O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, my dearest son, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came upon me to envision that I would complete it with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is much neglected in our region and has been entirely suppressed everywhere, the science has therefore perished and its strength lies only in the small descriptions found in books which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and the science is ignored.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I wish to revive her along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the shapes of the fire irons for cauterization and other instruments of the work with the arrangement of their declaration and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And therefore, whoever engages in this must rise to the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and how they move and remain at rest, and where their exit points are located.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, but with the work it is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that anyone who is not knowledgeable about the things said before should be careful not to fall into error and kill people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus have many wished in vain for these who meddle with this science but are abandoned without skill or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish physician who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman and cut the arteries in the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Therefore so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And another physician who removed a stone from a man's eye, the stone being large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	So he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to remove it, and saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they tried to cut into him he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And saw another physician who treated our duke whose leg was broken; and with the break there was a wound,
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the physician, full of ignorance, held the break upon the wound like stars with great force, and did not leave any bandage on the wound, leaving it thus until the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commanded that it should not be unbound,
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and so it remained until the leg was entirely swollen, and the foot went to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come unbind the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had unbound it, he felt at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the pathways of corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who burst an inflamed aposteme and then set it on fire through the wickedness of his ignorance.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is free from melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, surgery where there is danger in many situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore it is necessary that you guard yourself so that foolish physicians cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your weapons with confidence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through God's grace you may come to salvation and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave fearsome illnesses to those skilled in difficult cases;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove your weapons from what causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake the treatment of a serious illness unless you are summoned as a wise physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, arranged from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	And about the shapes of instruments, and the iron implements of cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cups and wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar matters;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And it is arranged with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and twists, and similar matters;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it is arranged from the head to the feet, with the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we begin discussing the work, it is necessary for me to describe the quality of each temperament and its benefit or harm.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of the patient and his harm are the longest speech and most subtle knowledge, and secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And about this spoke most of the wise men, and they agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And few are their words sufficient to me, for I dread length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery universally helps any complexion where there is matter, whether it be one of two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	That is to know, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a complexion that is both hot and dry with matter, some say that cautery is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	That cautery is not good for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot illnesses with heat, nor with dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And he who said the opposite said that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that occur in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and moisture of man to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not meddle with fire cautery except he who has experienced it, and knows through long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and the causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and the space of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other constitutions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians agreed upon the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, son: cautery along with fire is one of the secrets of cure and has greater benefit than cauterizing with burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not harm any other member if it is applied to the one being cauterized, except for those that are named otherwise.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Hot medications travel from limb to limb by dilation and cause severe illnesses there.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And sometimes they kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, due to its heat and goodness of substance, does not harm unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And these things I have found by experience and the length of service and study that I have devoted to this art, based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And therefore I apologize for the length of my speech, as I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that is hidden in fire and its qualities of operation, how it expels diseases from the body, as philosophers say when demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Take this into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	"And know, son, that they agreed upon when cauteries ought to be performed, and chose priests."
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	I say that cautery is beneficial at all times because the harm that comes from it is mitigated by its aid;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially, if a cautery is necessary for urgent pains that cannot wait until greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	For a disease healed by cautery has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and that is what they say;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they believe, because cauteries are not medicines that change complexion and dry up the humors causing pain; they are worth more than medicines for their speed of effect and power of operation.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And sometimes a disease comes upon a patient according to his complexion, the location of the disease, and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and excesses gather within him due to the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are applied where there is little excess or moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar treatments, from which such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the tail of medicine, which is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cauteries are worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are called the tail of medicine because when we administer methods of cure in any disease and they do not work, then we apply cautery, which is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	"So it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, but not according to the intentions of foolish physicians."
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries of gold are milder than those of iron, and they said this for the quality of gold and its preciousness.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the place of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have tried it and found that in some people, it is true.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauteries of gold are milder than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	Furthermore, when you heat a tool of gold, you do not know how hot it is just by its golden color, and it cools down quickly.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	And if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	If they put it on the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	Thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	"And for these reasons we use iron cauteries that we have better adapted to our work."
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	"Now I have arranged this chapter from beginning to end so that it may be easier to find."
dou cautere olivaire	"about the olive cautery"
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	"This cautery is beneficial for moistness and coldness on the head, and there are two kinds of it that are made because of an illness called 'sodicity' and because of many humors descending from the head to the eyes and ears, and for excessive sleepiness, toothache, sore throat, and especially all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, sciatica, apoplexy, and similar illnesses."
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a laxative drink for three or four nights, depending on their strength, age, and constitution.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then make him/her vomit at his/her head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	Then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his chest;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Afterward, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And where your middle fingers meet, apply pressure and then heat the cautery called 'olivary', of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	Place it on the marked spot, and move downwards while gently pressing your hand in a circular motion.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift your hand gently, and check if you see bone protruding slightly;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, then recommence the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Then take some wool, and put in softened cotton inside it, and place on the wound for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	then place a soft linen cloth soaked in butter on top;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave it on until the inflammation has subsided;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmacon' until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself;
et por ce si aide mues.	Therefore, change dressings often.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	"And some of these people say that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone and heal it."
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should leave the cautery on long enough and press hard enough to abrade as much bone as a thread used by women in their spindles, so that the humors may be expelled more freely;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and the wound should be left open for a prolonged period;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	then it should be dressed and bandaged.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be entirely good, except perhaps in some men where there is an appearance of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave this to him;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by prolonged, natural solutions as we have shown in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And even when the head of a patient is naturally weak, the first type of cautery seems safer and gentler to me, and it is this one that I now use together.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	"about chronic headache"
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When the head suffers from chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient should use ointments and pills called 'cochiae', and also remedies for the head, oils, and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And even if one performs the cautery we mentioned earlier, it is not helpful.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Be wary if the patient's head is strong in nature and is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize it with that cautery we mentioned earlier, but a little less intense.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards make a cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone as we have said before, and make one cautery at the place called "vessels";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	And that is the place where you apply cupping glasses;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	And raise your hand so that you do not see until reaching the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much greater pain with this cautery than with others; I will speak about it elsewhere.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And the cauteries on the horns must be more subtle than those used for cauterizing the middle of the head, and this is the reason:
dou cautere dou chief	"about the cautery of the head"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and extends to the eye, and the head is purged by moistifying medicines, and all the other treatments that I have mentioned in the section on diseases are applied, but none of it helps.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then apply cauteries in two ways: namely with hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with hot medicine is done by taking an almond and removing its skin, crushing it into a paste, applying it to both temples where the pain is felt, then making an incision in the temple so that you can place the almond paste under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is reset, then let it rest and hold it steady thus for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then release it and draw out the pain with garlic juice, leaving the wound thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply a piece of cotton soaked in butter until it can be pulled out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After applying the salve until it heals;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see that some medicines burning are needed, then treat them according to what I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery should be applied in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron from which this shape is made:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because its head is shaped like a hood with one small bend in the middle.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot; then hold your hand and gently rotate the fire until half of the blade of the heart-shaped end is heated.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Then lift your hand so that the artery does not burn; it is underneath, and much blood flows abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, apply cotton moistened with oil, placing it on the spot for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then I place moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is clean.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this hemorrhoid with the cautery called "cultellare," on its tip only, beware of touching the artery in this hemorrhoid that is not ancient.
de emigraine	of ulcer
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When treating hemorrhoids as mentioned earlier in the chapter on divisions of diseases, and it is not improving, and you see that the previously mentioned cauteries of medicine and iron do not help, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And seize upon the wound a line half the length of two fingers, and remove your hand once, ensuring that you do not touch the artery or reach the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the mandible that moves when chewing, and ensure that you only touch what moves, so that there is no spasming for the patient. Also beware of bloodletting from the artery when it is cut, or if cutting causes great fear, especially for someone who is not skilled or experienced in this matter.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And let the work remain unfinished.
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if these cauteries do not help the disease, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize it near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see this, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery, with a cautery that has two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And these cauteries are better and more helpful than those.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	For pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes to the ear, and one has opened there medications dissolving and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Then puncture all around the affected ear, or around both ears if the pain is in both, and move away a bit from the root of the ear, then mark the spot where you will begin.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make ten punctures around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it heals.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Only tortures which move with a flow of blood ought to be treated by cauterization.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not perform cauterizations on similar conditions that come from dryness and spasm of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When treating this condition of torturous movement with blood flow, and it is not effective through hydrides and purgations of the head and gargarisms, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the healthy appearing part, and make a cautery incision above the ear slightly below its horn, and another one on the temple about the length of a pea;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	And leave the cautery in place until half of the coal is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	This is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the knife we have placed before, but it is somewhat more refined, and the knives should be slightly thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the place as I said earlier, until it is clean.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one where it is called 'vessels' as we have said earlier, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And they should be treated as we have said earlier.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, give the patient large ointments and pills to cleanse the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	Then raise the head of the patient entirely, and place on the occiput the plaster of mustard that is written about in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the method of cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If he is healthy thus, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if he is not [healthy], apply three cauteries on him from the head down to the neck, placing each two fingers' breadth apart.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And treat it as you would others; and if you see them joining together, and the patient is suffering, apply one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if necessary, apply two more on the two horns, and treat until it is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And let the cautery that is called 'olivary' be like I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hairs and of what we have mentioned before
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After raising the patient's head, apply a cautery to it and to each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, apply four cauteries on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let him wait until the thickest hair has burned away; then raise your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the cure, once it is healed, use the cautery called 'olivare', which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilithic should only apply fire cautery to those who are phlegmatic. First, one must modify the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in previous sections when the patient is large and able to tolerate medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it's a child who cannot tolerate this, perform a gargle and chewing motion with softened foods often to cleanse the throat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	Then place the king's head in the middle, and perform the cautery as we have said before, and cauterize the vessel and each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and patient, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and weakness of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, using an olive-shaped cautery as I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, one should apply a single subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the excesses or corrupted moisture are caused by melancholy and produce thick phlegm, then apply as many cauteries as we have described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the excess is inclined towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist due to melancholy, then give them something to drink that cleanses the brain according to what is written earlier in this section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	Then place the head of the patient king;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a linen towel well-woven like a circle, and place it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient should sit cross-legged, being held firmly in all places;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Afterwards, present the linen, and use old sheep butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And warm it gently over fire so that the dough can bear being dipped into it.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Then empty the circle from within around the head and let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to the patient once each week with another good regimen until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize wounds by making several pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain increasingly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then place cotton dampened in butter and goose grease on top.
de l’awe des eulz	Here begins a chapter on the eye.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it first comes to the eyes as described in the division by signs I've mentioned, then begin and give the patient something purifying the head, keeping away all moistures, and make them sweat or take many baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Then he commands him to lay back his head and makes a cautery on the head, making two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the eye is in both eyes together, or one cautery if it is in one eye.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	Then cut all the veins and arteries that are below the heart with each cautery, making the cautery long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and the incision of cauterization, how you should stretch it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one makes a cautery or hot iron underneath the two hind legs.
dou cors des larmes	Regarding the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the forehead;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it is seen that they are due to cold, humid surplus, then one makes the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of the eyebrow descending towards the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	Make a cautery on the head, and two cauteries on each temple, and two cauteries or hot irons underneath the two hind legs.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if more is needed, then cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow at each small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Regarding the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the section on division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights of decoction of leeches.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king, burn with the iron where the olive oil cautery is made.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" on both sides, a little below the eyebrows.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	Be careful not to touch the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When paper made from oil is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the shape
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see fit, make two cauteries on both sides as long as the eyebrows are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not remove your hand until one-third of the paper has burned according to the method I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Regarding the eyelashes that touch the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the eyelashes turn inward and prick the eye, in which case cauteries are made in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Namely, either by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then put the patient on your knee;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After that, draw on the paper of the eyes a figure like the mirror of Myrtle, and let it be the beginning of the sign near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then put a ball of cotton soaked in egg white and powdered myrtle on the eye, then heat the cautery, which is shaped like this:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Then cauterize along the figure you have drawn, little by little many times, until the skin is burned at that spot;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of the health of the work is when you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up at the point of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then raise your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterwards the hairs grow back, and the paper becomes softened, then begin the cautery on that same spot again, just as you did at first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are lacking, cauterize them until the skin returns to its natural level, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	And for the burning medical cautery, instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even. Then make a template of parchment in the shape of a bay leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take equal parts (1 drachm each) of French soap and live coal ash, grind them together thoroughly;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make it quickly, so that it does not cool. Then spread the mixture onto your template in the shape of a bay leaf, and place it on the skin near the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	If the patient needs treatment for one eye only, work on that one; if both eyes are affected, treat them both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And place a moistened cotton ball under the eye.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And hold the patient's head steady in your hand. Place your two fingers on the medication and press gently. Move them every time the patient feels a burning sensation, as they will feel it like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine with your fingers.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting has passed, then lift the hot iron and see if the paper lifts as well, as it would have done by constraint of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	However, if not, then apply more of the medicine to the spot where it has not opened, so that your work is even, and your eyes sharp.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place softened cotton in butter until the heart's fire is extinguished; afterwards, dress the wound with ointment called 'dyafenis' and others, until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must guard your work carefully, so that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, then recommence the medicine on that spot softened by the paper properly, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after which dress it until it is healed
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the poultice for the eye:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that men's eyes differ in size and smallness, and according to this are your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the direct path should not be blocked for one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Here is the treatment for fistula by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in our divisions of diseases, but your treatment does not help,
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put their head in your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And have his servant hold his head between your hands so that it does not move or turn its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	Then put moistened cotton in egg white or in juice of purslane on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	Then heat the cautery which is shaped like this:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	And pointed at the head like the shape of a pigeon's feather, so that the cautery is sharp;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you wish, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it should also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	However, the one that is pointed is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Then press on the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, open it, and draw fire from the bowels
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Afterwards put the hot cauterizing iron on it, and keep your hand on the cautery at the side of the eye nearest the nose, so that your hand does not go mad.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then apply the cautery again once more, and do so a second time if necessary, and leave it on for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Then put on cotton moistened in butter, and continue the drying salve treatment until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, apply a corrosive ointment until the bone is exposed
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And follow the king's recipe according to what comes afterwards in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is another manner of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand that this is about a fistula, and find its location
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Then insert into the opening gently this thin thing: here is the form
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	And they do to the quantity of three-fifths of a penny.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	And hold your hand firmly over the wound, so that the patient does not move his nose at all, lest the molten lead flow into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient moistened cotton wool in an egg shell or in water;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead, if applied correctly, heals the site of the fistula, and the sinew by miraculous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer a probe to the nose and bring the fistula back to its proper place in the body of the nose.
des crevaices en levres	"for cracks in lips"
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur on lips which are called "hairs", especially on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks which we have mentioned in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat up a small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And quickly pour it into those cracks until it reaches the source;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then dress the site with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it becomes rotten and round, is inflamed, and turns into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said with incisions, but it does not help at all;
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Then you must apply the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the wound or opening of the fistula, keep your hand there until the hot iron reaches its bottom, and at the back of it.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this once or twice after the treatment that we have mentioned in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if it is cured thus, that is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	And if not, then you must expose the site and remove the rotted bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	on the mobility of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it is not effective, then place the patient's head in your hand;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	Afterwards heat the cautery whose shape will be described below so that you can put a band around the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and quickly place the hot cautery inside and hold your hand there until the patient feels heat reaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	Afterwards, remove your hand and continue using the cautery as you wish;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	Afterward, let the patient fill their mouth with salted water, and hold it for an hour with rich force.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And thus the moving tooth is made firm, and the softened gum constrained, and corrupt moisture dried.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	If toothache comes from coldness, where there is coldness or wind, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	And cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with butter is done thus: take fresh butter and put it on an iron or brass spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Then take cotton, wrap it around the tip of a tent (i.e., make it into a small cone), dip it in melted butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth; hold it until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And repeat this often until its effectiveness reaches the root of the tooth. Then, if you want to use cold butter and cotton, dip it in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and hold an iron heated over fire close enough for its heat to reach the bottom of the tooth without touching it.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauteries are of such kind that you should take one made of iron or brass, and it should be thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, of which the form will come later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter at the time of this cautery, and then apply the hot iron;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And perform a cautery on whichever head you wish, according to your ability.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the form of the cautery iron:
des scrophules	scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the hair cautery of which the form comes later, and it should have two openings for the smoke to exit from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	Place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice until it reaches the base of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its size, and leave it on for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	Place moist cotton soaked in butter until the burning sensation is gone.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, treat with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cauterizing iron:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels of the lungs, especially when it arises from a cold constitution, then the patient should be made to cough up phlegm first with solvent medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Afterward, apply a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go too high up towards the throat, and only singe it a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Afterward, apply another cautery at the junction of the neck and head of the spine, using the cautery called 'clavile' as shown above.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heal the joint as we have said before until it is whole.
de la toust	Here's how you can translate "de la toux" into English:
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	And when all diseases of the lung are from cold dampness, and the patient has no fever or cough, and the disease is chronic, then apply two cauteries to the fleshy part near the wound.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And place the second cautery between the breasts, between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And let the cauteries be of the type called 'clavile,' according to the shape described above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	If you see it, apply a cautery at its tip, that is called 'pointe,' of which the shape is described above in the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And let there be up to thirty points, or however many around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterward heal the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be of three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, perform them in three places.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the displacement of the shoulder joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture and is put back in place but cannot remain there and returns and dislocates again with even a small movement, as we have experienced it, then you must first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then have the patient lie on their back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the heart that is inside the titillation with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	And if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cautery that has two branches, the form of which is thus:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	And cauterize the lung until it pierces to the side, and bring the figure of the cautery together with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	And therefore cauterization is done with the cautery that has three rows, so that the figures of cauterization are six;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are arranged according to the fineness of a thread, and it is the form of the cautery that has three rows:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined onto this one nerve, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterwards place on the cautery pieces of broken porridge with salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	afterward let the patient rest and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavile, or many cauteries pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is sound.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach so that they alter its nature, and catarrh is multiplied in it, and usual methods of treatment do not help, then the patient must be turned onto his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then apply three cauteries to the lower part of the breastbone with the quantity of two fingers' width at each cautery on the upper end, and two cauteries outside the two ribs so that the figure of the cauteries forms a triangle with equal distance between them so they do not join together when they discharge pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the cautery burn so deeply that it reaches the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see cauterization with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing on the stomach one point according to the quantity that you see fit;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then cauterize with the entire cautery called 'the point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment that we have discussed previously, let it be without wound.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain comes from coldness and moisture and excessive windiness in the liver, so that it is greatly altered from its natural composition by excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and if the patient is treated with what we have said in division [treatment] and it does not help him, then the patient must be made to vomit.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	And place three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the ribs of the chest come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	And let there be space between each cautery equal to two fingers.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	And the cauteries on the long parts of the body should not have too much pressure applied from your hand throughout the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And only burn half of the skin, and let the patient lie down on their right side.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if they cannot do this, then they should lie down, extend their legs, and raise their arms.
et c’est li forme:	This is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your wish, then cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel if you are skilled and wise in this art; but be careful not to burn all of the skin, as you would dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And let it not come close to the eye, for the skin is very delicate there, and you will see this clearly.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the omentum:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it's within the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too intense.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is under the skin, extreme pain is felt.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	Then when this treatment fails according to doctors, the patient must be placed on their head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then press down on the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which here is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	Then cauterize with the cautery until the flesh is burned, and let it come to a boil until all the matter comes out.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After that, according to the cure of the roots until it's healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And only those who have studied medicine extensively for a long time should use this cautery, and through whom many of these diseases have been cured at least once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly act, nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Regarding the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that for pleurisy, cauteries made from the roots of aristologus should be used in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a long root of aristologus, as large as you can find and dry, and also thick and long like your two fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	And grind it in oil, and take it to the fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the navel and the neck, and make two small cauteries a little lower in the part that is below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And one cautery on the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on both sides of the breast below the cautery that is between the two shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand, but open it as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	Some ancient authors say that some people used to heat a cautery like a razor and place it between the ribs until it reached the boil.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And when it hurts, as we have said regarding the boil on the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula occurs which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Regarding the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse with the methods that we have said in the chapter on treatments, and it does not help, then there are three ways of cautery which are all good:
