des apostemes des levres	Of the swellings on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In many men, hard abscesses resembling peas in size, both small and large, occur within the lips
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then it is necessary that you turn back the lips, and cut open each nostril, take hold with tweezers, and cut in every part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then fill the place after the incision of crushed glass until the blood is staunched.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then dress it with a poultice, and dress the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often there appears on the flesh of the cheeks that which the ancients call "albulae";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	Then you must hold it with forceps and cut at its root, allowing the vein or blood to flow freely.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then place on the wound crushed glass or other powders that are restrictive and drying;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	And if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after cauterization
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	then these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Somewhat, sharp and ugly scales are gathered at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green, so much that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	therefore you should make the patient sit between your hands, their head in your lap, and remove the scales or tartar from the teeth until none remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and likewise do for blackness and greenness, yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if you remove what is there due to the first cause, it's good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then start again on the second day and the third, until all is removed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth require various shapes of tools to scrape them according to what the work shows, because the scrapers used to clean between the teeth have different shapes from those used to remove tartar from the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And let these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay extraction as long as possible, for it should not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to extract it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constricted by a draught, you must be certain of the throbbing tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain leaves the patient and they believe it was in the good tooth that is extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	yet still the pain does not leave due to this, for we have seen many times that the bad one remains.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary to scrape around the tooth with a strong spathula to protect the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it gently between your two fingers or with fine forceps until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And keep the patient's head steady between your knees while you hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these tools and place it gently on each side, and with the lever move it as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if a tooth is pierced and swallowed, you must fill it with bandages where the hole is.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and gently extract it with forceps so that it does not break while being extracted;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and much bleeding must be caused around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And make sure you do not break it, and if a piece remains, it will return to the patient through the wickedness of the root causing even greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act as foolishly as some hasty and reckless surgeons who sometimes break the jawbone and thus fail to achieve what we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause serious illness through their carelessness due to roots left behind or a broken jawbone, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	If bleeding occurs afterwards, which often happens, then apply powdered vitriol to the area;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the tools with which you first move the teeth should be long-pointed and thick-hafted so that they do not double over when you pull the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	And these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	"And let them be of heavy members so they do not bend at all during the pulling, and let them be of good iron well-made, and let them have teeth for holding moves."
de la racine des dens	"from the root of the teeth"
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains during extraction, you must place cotton soaked in honey on the spot for one or two days until the spot becomes softened; then insert the tweezers called 'algefri', from which the head seems like a bird's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should also be made inside like a file, and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali," that is, tweezers, this is the form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break; and if the root comes out through it, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	But if not, then help yourself with all the tools, of which their forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are placed on the surface of the teeth, and this instrument resembles large pliers, here is its form
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this tool be strong so that it cannot break; and know that there are many tools for teeth;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other tools which are not counted here.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise master finds his own instrument, according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if one breaks a limb or other bones where it is useful, then he seeks the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-fastening to hold the bone, so that it does not slip away, but can hold and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore to its place with appropriate medications, and if there is rot in the bone, even if it is small, remove all this equipment:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural course, and their form is ugly, especially in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is near behind the tooth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be removed or filed:
adonques lou raie;	Therefore cut the ray;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is next to the tooth, take this instrument of which here is the shape, like a small beak, and let it be made of iron well-sharpened on top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently tap with your hand every day for the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent so that one can file it, then use a file like this whose form is like
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And file the tooth gently bit by bit over several days until it falls out without moving.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then level it at the end with any sharpener, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, then file down its sharpness until it is even so that it does not wound the tongue nor impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When a tooth before the eye is knocked out, either by blow or fall, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without it falling out, even after treating them with medicines that restrict it.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then you must bind it with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold does not change.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let my son's thread not be too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth aligned, then take the thread and pass it through both healthy teeth, placing the heads between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until blood flows up to the neighboring healthy tooth.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then resume the wrapping up to where you began, and hold your hand gently but firmly, so that it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the heads of the thread with pliers, join them together, and pass them behind the healthy tooth, placing it so that it does not injure the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave it tied as tightly as possible until it can remain in place; and if it becomes loose or the thread rots, tighten it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains thus and serves in this manner throughout its lifetime, that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two upper teeth and the two lower ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, replace it in its position little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let not the ignorant and impatient meddle with it; sometimes a tooth shape made of cow bone is used, placed in the position where there is a gap, secured as we have said, and remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this tie comes under the tongue by nature at birth;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or through an accidental wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	And the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and place their head on your knee, raising the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve ligature from behind, until the tongue is freed from its attachment; and if there is any hardness or knot, which is from a wound scar, insert the nail and cut it from behind;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	And ensure that the cut is not too deep, lest the artery beneath be harmed.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	Then lift the wound with rosewater and salt or cold water, then place a linen bandage beneath the tongue
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And have the patient apply it every night so that the wound does not close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if blood oozes from the wound, then place powdered vitriol on it
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood dries, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this purpose
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another cure until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see a streak of black or hard colour, which the patient does not feel, do not touch it, for it is cancer
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it tends towards blenching and there is moisture present, then cast on the ointment called Onction, make an incision with a subtle spatula, and draw off the matter from both sides
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	If your blood becomes faint during your work, then place powdered vitriol upon it until it stops flowing, then return to your task until you have drawn all the fire.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then raise the lever of earth and stone, and heal with other remedies until he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	Throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes into the throat come stones called 'godath', which are properly called tonsils, and when you treat them as we have said in our discussion, if they are not healed, then be aware:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If they are hard boils with a small opening and dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also for the letting out of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it alone until it is ripe, and then you will break it off, or it would burst on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of pale color with a slender root, then prepare the instrument for cupping, but first make sure that the boil is warm and has softened.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his limbs in your hand, and he opens his mouth and the servant takes it between his hands, and presses the tongue from below with all the instrument; this is the form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And let it be of silver or refined brass like a sharp knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the hot cautery iron and insert it into the almond, and pull it out upwards as much as you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And bring some cloths with you, then wipe the instrument clean; this is the form that resembles forceps.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And moreover, their heads are curved and one towards the other, and they are very sharp, made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use pincers, of which here is the shape
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have incised one of the almonds, then incise the other in the same manner; afterwards, the patient should gargle with warm water and salt water, and if there is bleeding, he should gargle with warm water and pomegranate rind or myrtle leaves boiled, until the blood is staunched.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then [apply] the treatment until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses are born in the throat besides the tonsils, so cut them thus like the tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale because of the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if this had lasted for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was already so swollen that it had pushed out both ears through the nostrils
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore acted quickly and inserted a probe into the one boil, then drew it out forcefully, and drew out a large portion of pus.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I inserted again into the other hole that had grown, and opened its mouth and pressed on its tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards, inserting the probe into these abscesses and cutting one part of it open, only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the woman's throat passage was opened up, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting this abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the boil crisscrossed often, filling again the space I had emptied, becoming very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Therefore I pierced and cauterized it inside its core:
ensi demora sens croistre;	So it remained without growing further;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I departed from these parts, not knowing what God did with him afterwards.
de l’uve	The eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and protuberant, it is called 'perpendicular';
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is below, thick and round, it is called 'eye'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the section on cutting, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the large boil has healed over but the inflammation persists, then you must lance it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And the one that is rounded together and not protuberant;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and if it is red in color or blackish, you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient thereby.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore necessary, when you see it in the manner I have described regarding its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit facing the sun and press his tongue with the instrument whose memory we made before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it under, and cut with the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two membranes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut any further than the natural limit beyond which there is excess;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you cut more, it harms both sight and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, apply what we have said in the incision of the two membranes, until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, you must use a device for cauterizing that fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is necessary that the patient place their head in your hand, and then press the tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize it with hot iron, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And here is the shape of this instrument:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And at its head there is a hollow where one places the medicine, like the bowl of a spoon, and places the instrument with all the medicine on the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And let the patient lie on their side such that saliva and mucus from their mouth flow towards the medicine within, so it does not descend to the throat, and avoid drinking.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it darken and the pain from the medicine has ceased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	If you see this, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton at the corner of the eye until the cotton touches the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and it will fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, do so, and afterwards wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be washed with cold water, and let it be cured by gargling until it is clean.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incising or using a cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and celery and similar herbs, gather them all or some of them into one pot, place it on the fire, and let it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pot should be well covered with clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument for removing hair like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end of the instrument should be placed in the patient's mouth until the steam rises to the eye through the canal until the eye is destroyed;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards, repeat this often until the eye dries out; but be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot boil, as many things can happen then.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not make fire except for the declination of an abscess boil.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put in its head an eggshell so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the eggshell does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times something sharp like bone or fish spine, or anything else, gets stuck in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So then you pull out what you can see, and press down on the tongue with the instrument so that you can see the object move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you cannot see and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	Perhaps then the object will come out through vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of nail, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	Then bind the sponge with thread, and then suture it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when it comes to its place, it will harden, and then draw out fire;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come forth as we have said, then take the instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter into the throat, and have its head raised upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and ensure you do not touch the epiglottis so that it does not close over everything, nor push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And have the patient move the instrument there so that they may know where the thing is hardened;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	So push it down until the place is drawn out evenly along the entire length of the instrument.
de la sansue de la gorge	de la sansue de la gorge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the sinew is healed as I have mentioned in the division, by the treatment with medications;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, and then press their tongue with the instrument I have mentioned to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, then treat it with a small iron pin or with fine forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a headed cane and put it into the throat of the patient, and then put red-hot iron on the head of the cane, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full handful of cold water, open the mouth, tilt it back without swallowing, and move it with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood senses the water, it flows out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not flow out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with incense, using the same instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall without fail.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is this: take a pot with live coals in it, and cover the pot with a cloth pierced in the middle, and insert the head of the instrument into that hole.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then throw in your incense, and the patient puts the end of the tube in their mouth, closes their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes straight to the blood.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the blood will flow out, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And the patient suffers thirst, and consumes salted and sour foods, and should not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Therefore, it will then be necessary for her to discharge it through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the tonsil looks like curved tongs for entering into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and resembles a goose's beak and has sharpness of a rasp, such that what it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	And here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many similar kinds of abscesses are described, according to what memory brings forth here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And there are two ways in which it resembles itself and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where abscesses are located on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	However, some abscesses should not be pierced until the bowels have completed their function.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are others that must be pierced as soon as they form and do not wait for completion, like those near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and they are left until they have rotted around, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When an abscess is near the main member,
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	If they prick at their base, pierce them before they grow.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not necessary that you pierce a boil that has grown without first digesting it, except for those near the base, so they do not go too deep and become an internal fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And it may take a long time to heal.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you should know the stage of the boil's perforation that has grown according to its completion, which is when the pain ceases and the fever subsides, along with the decrease in pain and redness, and the flattening and hardening of the head of the boil, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary that you make the incision where the boil depends the most and where it opens more easily;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And the incision should be long in proportion to the body, and if the boil is on the hands or feet, or in joints, near arteries, and in all similar places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those cases where they affect, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better that you delay perforating until it is confirmed with digestion completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before then, the body will be filled with its venom, and is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps harden the lips and deepen its wound.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many cracks according to the likeness of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to dig with the cautery and cover
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when they have become like the scales of a dragon, and are softened, then you must do as one does for boils.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such ones that are split into three corners, and those whose covering is like the skin of a mullet, as abscesses of angels
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such ones where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like soft superficial abscesses, you must pierce them plainly
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when an abscess is large, and it has collected much bowels, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bowels at that hour, but draw out a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again afterwards;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times gradually, until all the bowels come out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying a child, or small infants, or elderly feeble men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps at the release of the bowstring, which by chance causes the death of the patient, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore leave this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then examine the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a clean cut, then bring clean linen or old cotton bandages;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it is a large abscess and there are many holes in it, then you must put into each one a bandage so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut off a part of the skin around an abscess, and you have shaved it around, then you must fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the dressing, and apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if flows of blood occur during your procedure, then bring cold water and towels, wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, then apply dressings and treatment, and the powders that I mentioned elsewhere in this book; and if it is during wintertime, and the location of the wound or abscess is very nervous, then you should place wet bandages and cloths on it, warmed in wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in summertime, and the location is fleshy, then you must place wet bandages in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the abscess, cleanse it, and dress it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this, he must universally recognize in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is that chapter.
des soros	Here are some translations of the word "soros" from Middle French to English:
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head meets the neck come small abscesses, resembling those of chickens in their skin, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some thick ones and such where there is moisture like poultices;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are those that are hard and bony in appearance, and there is no doubt if the artery opposes them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you should test all instruments called 'entromissoire', from which the form comes later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, then close it with a long stitch.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, scrape it off without leaving any of the skin that contains it, because it returns again if anything is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian unguent, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not that, use water and salt, and dress the wound until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And these are what remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then start again with cotton as before on the second day and the third, until you know that there is nothing remaining from the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound with appropriate ointment until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if an abscess holds much matter inside, cut it according to this shape, with a long incision
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cast your incisions, and scrape off all the skin around it, and focus all your effort on drawing out what lies beneath the skin
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do for an abscess if it is hard, and with cutting and dressing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting of a hard and moist abscess is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And also for those abscesses that have no moisture at their head, and especially for those hard ones that I cut from the head of an old woman
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	I found the abscess to be like a hard, rough, white stone, which could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had tried to break it, they would have done as much harm as striking a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	For other abscesses that come at the head, especially those that appear on the heads of children and the roots of ears, open them always in the lowest position possible, so that the boil can easily come out
et les cure si com il covient.	And heal as it is necessary.
des scrophules	scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin; sometimes they also come elsewhere on the body, and there are many of them, and they intertwine with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	Each boil is properly within its own skin, such as the pimple on the forehead and the abscess on the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And similar sorts of boils are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others malignant that refuse to yield to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	Therefore, the one that you see has a good constitution to touch, and is similar in color to the body, moves from every side and is not hard against the veins of the neck nor against the artery or the passage, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	So you should cut it from above, scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart wound apart if necessary, as we have said regarding head abscesses;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And cut little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor should the scalpel be too sharp or cutting deeply, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, then place powdered vitriol or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and press the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then check your finger for any small scabs, and cut them off and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, it is not necessary to cut off that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then fill the wound with Egyptian ointment-soaked cotton, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scab, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up tightly; for there will be no excess left due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must understand to cover the root of it, and draw fire, and the cut as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scabs that are full of fluid, pierce where they burst open;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it as that mentioned earlier, depending, then bring bandages with salve and similar things so that it rots what remains of the rot.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleaned, apply a salve to the flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	de squinance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with coughing fits, it is necessary that the fold of the throat called 'epiglottis' be cut away;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and do not provide assistance to those who have hot abscesses in the mouth or throat, as all their veins and pores are open.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we do so below three circles or four a small cut across, between two circles or through the quantity of the cut of the soft palate, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are so attached to the epiglottis that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long on either side.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the neck all around, then cut open the chest until he reaches the breastbone;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then sever the esophagus as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the cutting of the windpipe at the breastbone that blood flows from the broken place and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And once the danger of strangulation has passed, join together the two lips of the wound in the chest and sew it up without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medications that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked off, and the patient is judged to be near death, and his breathing has failed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut off the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow and breathe through the wound, thus avoiding death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore the ancients commanded that the wound be kept open until the worst of the illness has passed; this usually takes three or four days. Then they commanded that the wound be stitched and dressed until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that the blood issuing from it was not from the veins or arteries but only from the throat, and the breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastily cleaned and dressed the wound until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And after some days, her voice returned to normal, and she recovered her usual appearance;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This type of abscess is called 'hernia of the throat' and appears as a large, dark bruise, common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	And it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	by nature and by accident.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Nature has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents occur in two ways: one is like a bruise, the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear involved, but one should not operate with fire cautery except in the case of a small [abscess], and prove and search this throughout the entire introvertor:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a hard tumor and not connected to any vein, cut it like a boil and treat it entirely with its cover if there is one;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well all around, and cure it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of tumors, which I will describe in detail;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must explain the difference between a tumor and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an ulcer is warm and has fever until the boil bursts, and then decay is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without heat or fever or pain, and contains the lymph, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a sieve, and becomes swollen;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are similar to either fat or moisture, and most have the colors as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When treating a fatty tumor, it is necessary to first examine and express the contents using an instrument called the 'intromittor', according to the shape described in the following chapter."
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of examining the abscesses in the nose is that you take the moistest part that you find in the abscess and twist your thumbs little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the center, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the trocar, and beware lest anything spurt forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist pus runs forth, whatever its color may be, open it as I have said of other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the trocar no moisture comes forth, know that it is fat; therefore cut it in crosswise and take it with forceps, and scrape it lightly from each side and beware of the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the lymph;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	But if anything remains, the pain will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if a little remains and the blood grieves you, then apply to the wound some corrosive waters, bind the wound, and put on cooling remedies for the heat of the wound, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the pain is great, cut open both lips of the wound, and treat those that enter the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if a beating vein is opposed to you or another, quickly apply powdered vitriol to the place and leave it for two or three days until the wound rots, and let the blood's ebullition rest.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to cauterize what remains of the pain.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the shapes of intrusive instruments, and they come in three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	Big, medium, and small
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are 3 squares called 'albaret', and 1 called 'breb', and they come in three varieties
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small to surround fistulas
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used to suture wounds, and they are made of brass, iron, or silver; those that are yellow are most valued, and they are especially praised for surrounding fistulas
et sont de III manieres:	and they come in three varieties
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small according to the size of the hole's width
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the needles are very similar, as you can see here
grans, moiens, et petis;	Large, medium, and small
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are also needles with two curves in three varieties
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are needles with three curves, which also come in three varieties
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are needles with two curves and needles with one curve only, both of which come in three varieties
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these instruments are cutting; there are some that cut only on one side, from which the nerves are stripped off so as not to cut the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	Among these instruments are also spoons inserted into handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds of them:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium-sized, as you can see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	Use them only on smooth skin, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar areas;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	Sometimes another small instrument is used, resembling the skin of fists, in this shape, with which blood is wiped away:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the location where veins and arteries are severed or where there has been excessive bleeding. Sometimes they are made in this larger size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they begin to be corrupted until they resemble women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	And who wants to treat them should do so according to this form from line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strip away the fat, dress the wound with salve containing flesh powdered fine, then bring together the two lips of the wound for stitching, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the breast tilts downward and is large like in women, cut it into two along the two similar creases above.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape:.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders as necessary until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let him suck until he consumes the remainder and the fat, then heal it until it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	"Abscesses of the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"The abscesses that occur under the arms are usually hard tumors resembling scrofula or have rough surfaces, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the boil has been drained out, then fill the wound with soft cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and dress it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the boil resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have said for scrofula wounds, and if the wound fills with pus again, then apply a cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is cut, and the skin above it is cauterized, abscesses often form; likewise when a vein is inflamed and becomes abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	If one recognizes this, then if it is for the artery, the abscess will be long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel it with your fingers, there will be extraction.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	When it is due to the vein, red appears around the opening.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and angles of the jaw and neck, and in many other places; and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the cautery of iron, and especially for one who is at its head; also for one that is swollen from an artery cut through the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the incision widely, carefully separating the artery from the tissues until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then place a needle beneath one side and pierce it through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have shown you regarding the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then prick the spot between the two ligaments with an intrument until blood comes out of it; and let the abscess be drained.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply pressure to the outer thigh until the ligament drops.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is due to the cutting of a vein, then you must squeeze whatever you can from the abscess towards all the skin, then place the needle beneath the spot where you are holding it and pierce it through; and let there be one doubled thread so that you may draw it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie off the abscess as I have told you, with the ligament of one of two parts using a thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not on fire, then insert another needle underneath all the thread beneath the incision of the first needle, and pinch the threads at four places;
