puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about fractures of the head later on.
de la plaie dou col	"of the neck wound"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy but to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not apply anything cold to the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuity extends to the brain, which is the highest organ.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medication be warm, such as hot water washed in warm water mixed with rose oil and cooked likewise in warm water, and other mineral stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then suture and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if wounds are deep and blood has gathered and is full of bowels, then pierce it below or even lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and blood flows profusely, then dress it, bandage it, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut or the heart, and the windpipe is guarded so that the flesh goes there, then cut the heart from the throat's artery, but do not touch the throat; rather, reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then constrain it carefully, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with warm compresses until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has impressed upon the bone, then scrape it away.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can; if not, leave the wound to suppurate until it is dressed and drained.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones and fistulas in the wound, then treat it as I said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"on wounds from a lance or a dagger"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a cut from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if wind comes out of the wound as the patient breathes.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep but full of fresh blood, do not apply the powder at first nor bind it so that the blood does not flow too deeply and reach the heart, killing the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment and bandage it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, place damp cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	So that there will be no spasm, nor harmful trembling of the heart, nor shortness of breath;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these favorable signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with splints and other treatments until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot heal or close, know that there is a fistula present;
si la cure si com on doit.	If the treatment is performed as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and is simple, whether on the front or back, then treat the one that is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, stitch it;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, use powder; and if it is close to the bone and has taken chips of bone, clean the wound, and treat any broken bones;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not broken, leave the wound to fester until it is ready for extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"on rupture of the abdomen"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	Abdominal pain can be severe, moderate, or mild;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes with a large wound, the intestine or mesentery jumps out,
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the stitching is more difficult; sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because if one puts too many intestines back in place, unless they are put back together carefully.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Therefore, the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold, causing them to return too soon; thus, it is better to move the wound slightly so that one can put the intestines back in place correctly rather than in other ways.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a hole in the belly comes about in four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The first two are common stitches that occur during abdominal surgery; the other two stitches for wounds on other parts of the body are also common in other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Yet they are more suited to abdominal surgery, and I will discuss each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, nothing of the intestines has spilled out, and there is little need to repair it, this can be done in one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	For due to the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when he is cold, warm him in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Soak a sponge or soft cloth in hot water only, or cook in boiling water with cumin and cypress seed, and warm the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this restricting wine is made, and it is believed to help reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling begin to subside, then moisten the intestines with water in which alfalfa and mallow have been cooked, for by this means the entrance is eased somewhat;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it still cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with an instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first cure is believed to be better than the cut, so none should cut without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for splitting [it]:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you cut within the curve and do not go beyond it, see here its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, then carefully replace them according to their natural form in their proper place if you have the power, for this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and located below the belly, you must make the patient lie on his back and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if it is located below the belly, raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts; likewise, if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, make sure that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus you must arrange what I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, put on what you are equipped with, then have between your hands one cloth moistened with which you gently wipe the entire wound and bring together the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common way of suturing: first take one or more needles according to the quantity and width of the wound, then leave two spaces from the beginning of the wound, and attach a strong thread to the needle.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two heads of skin with the two heads of sinew, which are underneath the skin within, until you make it pierced from that part, and join the two heads of sinew together in fours.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then tie a doubled thread around the needle on both sides, then bring together the two heads of the wound evenly, and leave two spans apart, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing so according to what you need needles for, until all the wound is constrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cut through all flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore they must be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And do not push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it is sewn.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then cut the heads of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping; and place tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to keep them still until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, where only one or two needles are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, which involves sewing the two heads of skin and the two heads of flesh together with one needle having a medium-strength thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And once you have pierced all three heads together, then draw the needle back to where you started, in the manner that one sews cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	Leave the thickness of a barleycorn between each stitch.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch closes the wound; I sewed a wound that one man had in his belly, which was cut by a knife and was more than a palm's length wide, and it opened to expose two palms' worth of intestines.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestines after it had been twenty-four hours since the blow, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, which I dressed, and it remained healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians judged that he would die, but it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and twice daily I placed old cotton on the wound and washed it with honey water until it was clean.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it from the outer part to the inner.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the heart from right to left, then place the end of the silk thread where you inserted the needle and pierce it on the other side from inside to outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the meaning of this stitch is that you should sew like a furrier sews furs, leaving the silk thread once on one side and taking it up again on the other until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes specifically, is as follows: some people join the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the suture to the other in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stitch a needle at the near end of the thread and pierce only that spot, leaving both ends of the suture.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part until it reaches the inside, at both ends of the suture.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce both ends again from the outside to the inside in two other places near each other on the other side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the best and most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen also says that one should suture the abdomen with two needles each having thread on them
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must insert one needle on this side and the other on that side in the manner of those who sew leather
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know this: when the ulcer is inside the belly, then the stitching is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the art has moved it, then reset the intestines and the stitch.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put powder around the flesh, and if the wound has moved, then put some ointment that is available, so that the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And cut the thread, and may the lips be closed, and the edges.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound like others until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicines, then put on cotton wool soon after it begins to discharge, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many dispositions when wounds are simple, you need no other medicine;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the main members, then it is necessary to moisten clean linen in warm rose oil or rose oil and place it around the angles and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or corruption in his bowels, and this happens often, then apply black wine enemas, especially if the corruption reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce within it, knowing that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	Injuries to the intestines called 'jejunum' cannot heal, due to the thinness of their vessels and the delicacy of the entire body, and their closeness in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	If the bowel protrudes from the wound, then push it back in as with the intestines while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and turned black or green, then tie off the black part to prevent blood flow, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the tie, and place the two ends hanging down from below the wound until it reaches far to facilitate the extraction when the bowel drops, and the wound gapes.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are wound around each other, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I have seen that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and the digestion and wind passed through it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment as best I could there, and did not cease to cleanse until he was free of infection, and the area was sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healed, I worried that the patient might have some injury in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but there was no harm, he simply remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take a thread with large knots, then bring the lips of the wound together, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it pulls its mouth shut.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then he cuts off the head, and this is held so that it cannot be untied; then he puts another stitch afterwards in this manner as before until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	Then close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	Such a head will harden in the intestines and cause no harm to the patient, and the intestines can be tied with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this intestine thread that is very lean, and then tie at its end a thin twisted linen thread; then insert the thread into the needle and stitch up the intestine, and draw it back together.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this manner of sewing with stitches is used only according to trustworthy and hopeful ways;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, then there is no remedy or health except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"whether it is a fistula or wherever it may be,"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows large, is universally called "fistula," and likewise when it becomes hollow and sinks inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is truly a broken vein, hard and white, where there is no pain felt, and it is also called like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes it appears clear and thin, but other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes small, and other times quite large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not clean and has no flesh, appears only through one of the eight causes.
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	That is to say, because of the thickness of blood or flesh.
ou por sa malice;	Or due to its wickedness.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that prevents flesh from forming.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	'Or when there is too much bile.'
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or where the place is putrid, and the matter is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Or because the medication used for treatment is not good.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	'Or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence.'
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or because the property in that region is slow digestion, delayed healing, and naturally inflamed.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal remedies in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now it is fitting that I tell you about the cure of fistula which is done by manual work:"
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	A fistula happens in every limb of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the face, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And there are some that come from the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are like this are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance involved;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment, and you recognize it, then take a tent of lead or iron, apply it to the fistula.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is twisted, search it with a subtle probe of lead, for lead bends around the twistiness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot search it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture will pass from one hole to another and cleanse it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then squeeze it as hard as you can to see if there is bone or nerve inside it, and how deep it goes. Ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press your hand on it, and where they feel it most.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And once you know truly where it is and if it is far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein or in any of the places I told you about, then cut according to what I told you, and remove the fracture and the rotted flesh that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then treat it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep in the right place, you must cut as deeply as you can, and then insert moist probes soaked in hot water into the fistula up to its head, so that the medicine corrode the excess flesh remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I apply dressings made from holy flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it does not heal with this [treatment], then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotted by the fistula, cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not trouble you in the main members [limbs], as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed and there is decay and blackness, scrape it until all the decay is removed, then dress it with holy flesh until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it does not heal, return again as before; know that you have not yet reached the source:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	So uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore it to its proper place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it heals thus, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	But if not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other means but to let nature take its course
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small rotten bone and you can grasp it with forceps, then extract it with the appropriate tool; but if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving none behind
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if moisture is causing harm and there is no error or fear, then cut away the moisture, flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something irritating on the wound to cause decay around the bones; then when the place has rotted around the bones, they will come out more easily
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone like that of the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone; then restore the wound
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is much decay and it reaches close to the surface of the bone
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	Then it should be cut all the way down to the decay, and then cured until it is solid.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	A young man around 30 years old had pain in his leg from an internal cause. Matter accumulated in the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, but there was no apparent reason to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the foolish doctors insisted on opening it until the abscess ruptured, releasing much matter. It became a fistula with many holes through which bowels and pus from the body discharged.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	For two years many doctors tried to treat it, but none with any skill in the art of medicine. I was called in and saw his leg and the remedies they were using, as well as what was flowing out through the holes in great quantity.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man's body became red, with a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	So I hurried and cut into one of the holes until I exposed part of the bone. It was found to be decayed and perforated, with corruption reaching the inner bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw those which appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption besides that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And began to dress the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but could not heal it.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then resumed [the treatment], and discovered the bone as before, and found that the corruption had spread to the bone itself, and I removed it, and tried to heal the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	Yet still I could not, so I cut around about a palm's breadth of bone, and removed it entirely, then dressed the wound with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was soon healed and sound, but the patient could not endure further treatment due to his weakness, and because of his fear of death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the purpose of bloodletting was often performed, but he was entirely healed afterwards, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and he was of good disposition and had no harm nor contradiction at all, neither oncoming nor departing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be treated thus:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take linen, and bind it tightly at the end of the exposed bone, and instruct him to stretch his arm upward;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And place another linen bandage, thicker than the first, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone, so that you pull out the corrupt flesh underneath and uncover the flesh on the spot where the wound should be, so that the bone does not ulcerate the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place a stick or a board underneath the bone to move the corrupt flesh away.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And this should be done until one can see and feel the corruption, and again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	If the bone is corrupted but does not appear open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then place a stick underneath, and then scrape the corruption from one side to the other with a spoon that is as long as the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	If the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint and scrape the bone that contains it from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than surgery.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if corruption is at the wrist of the hand or the ankle, it is very serious indeed, but nonetheless you must investigate that corruption and how it appears.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	Cleanse it in every way possible, provided that neither vein nor nerve opposes you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that there are many kinds of saws and needles for cutting these bones according to the position of the bones and their appearance from within, as well as their thickness, fineness, length, shortness, and hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore one must prepare each tool suitable for its respective operation.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that your work will show you which tool you need according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Therefore, choose the tool you need based on what is appropriate for it.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head swells either due to internal cause or due to lack of heat;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And once you have treated that inflammation with medication and remedies, but they are not beneficial, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to the point where the inflammation begins, so that the patient escapes death or the greater harm of losing the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the sign is that the limb becomes black as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, this corruption then spreads from limb to limb, affecting the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Therefore, hasten to amputate, especially if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures like marine scorpions or snakes and similar ones; but if the corruption has reached the joint of two fingers, then cut there, but do not allow it to progress up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, amputate at the joint so that corruption does not spread to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the elbow, death ensues, and no amount of external remedies can help by their power.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	Similarly happens when corruption comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes to the heel, cut off the whole heel.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	The manner of cutting off or cauterizing the limb is thus: tie it above and below, extend one assistant downwards along one of the ties, and another upwards along the other tie, and cut away the flesh between the two ties with a broad-bladed knife until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or cauterize it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy flesh, lest another injury and abscess occur to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood flows during your operation, cauterize the wound immediately, applying some powder that stops bleeding.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medication until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a man in sum pity:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a blackening appeared on him as if burned by fire, and this corruption first came upon his right foot, spreading to cover the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he quickly covered his foot with a copper plate, and it healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	Many years later the corruption returned on his right hand, and he came to me. After cleansing his body, I applied things that reflect heat, but the corrosion did not stop.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to because I still hoped to drive back the matter with reflection.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the virtue of man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he despaired altogether and returned to his land, and hurried to cover his hand, and he recovered.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have heard this told only for the purpose that one may do otherwise when there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a very tender place and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of bowel.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it becomes round and breaks open, and the bowel jumps out, and the place remains empty, like an old vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that is above it is also as thin as delicate cloth, and does not reach down to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called 'sound,' and is not called 'fistula'.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it extends so far that it reaches to the bone and goes deep, then it is called 'fistula'.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And you must cut around this skin, especially when it is thin, just like a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	But do not worry about its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you suspect that the skin will spoil, but the decay is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then prepare a clyster like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breast is large and the bowel emitting it has a foul odor, then use an Egyptian clyster made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take equal parts of hellebore, oil, and litharge, and cook them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	Then take what you need according to your requirement, mix it with water and honey, and use it for a clyster on the breast, closing the anus.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Repeat this many times until the breast is cleansed and the foulness is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And sometimes water with ashes is used for a cleansing when this medicine is not present; you should take ashes of vine wood, pour on water, then strain it, and use it as an enema until you know that the breasts are well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the water with ashes, then use an enema of water and honey, with a little bit of ground orpiment.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you may use an enema of honey and mixed wine, for the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the blood thinner.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And once you have done this and are confident that the breasts are well cleansed, then use an enema of what causes flesh to be born there; you should take emplastrum diachilithon and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you may use an enema of some medicines and ointments, the properties of which I have mentioned when treating about ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	If the hole of the breast is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter it, then enlarge it slightly with an iron tool, and place a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the wound is too wide, leave only enough skin to allow for the insertion of the clyster tube, and if the hole that the bowel throws up is above, cut it lower down or where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowels are deep, do not allow any flesh to intervene;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cut the breast below as you see it, then prepare in such a way that the bowel runs to its lowest point, for when the bowel is deep, do not allow any flesh to intervene; and if you cannot cut the breast below as you see it,
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowel may run easily downward, leaving nothing of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take medicines to consolidate for placing on the wound, they are placed on the linen cloth which covers all of the wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cut as far as you can around the hole of the breast with a larger cut than the first one, then apply soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the wound to alleviate the pain, but do not remove the outer large cloth until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And the one on top of the hole of the breast removes often to remove the pain, and know what comes out of the wound, whether it is venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when this medicine has spread in such a way you see what kind of matter comes out of the wound, then know that the breast has already healed, and the health approaches.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change the bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	"And if after many days the breast still discharges undigested bowels, know that the breast has not yet healed."
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are contracted after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose flesh wounds take too long to heal, and those that heal too quickly;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested food jumps suddenly from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach is not functioning properly;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the stomach is slow to digest and is distant from its proper state, apply drying medications that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as diaphanous ointment, for it contains much vitriol, which is the final medication.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphanous ointment, and they make it with rose oil, and rose water equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	Then mix it together and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And similarly, cooked honey is more effective when diaphanous ointment is not available. Take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense, grind them together, and powder them onto the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then glue the drapell, and stretch it over the breast, and sometimes one administers an aristologus longum, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like powdered centory.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simples or of compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them and make powder of it, and put on the honey that I have said, and use
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption has gone deep, causing an impression on the bone in hard members or joints
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand, or foot, or sometimes arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is neglected and becomes old, then a hard abscess forms, which cracks and swells so much that it reaches the root of the nail, sometimes even cracking the entire nail
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Corrosion reaches the bone, causing foul-smelling pain; the thigh is doubled over, and the skin appears ashen.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bones are healthy, and the nail is sound;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to prick, and the sore appears, then you must place a hot iron under the nail that pierces the flesh, and hold it there; carefully cut away the affected flesh and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion reaches the bone, cut it away and cauterize with fire, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see that both are corrupting, cut them off at their base just like what was mentioned before, then treat until they are healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if he is wounded, impaled, and feels great pain, then you must heal him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the corner of the nail at an angle using a pair of scissors, but be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, then put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are sometimes found in some men's hands by chance are entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is bone or claw, and sometimes they arise from the root of the joint, where the birth is on some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born with a knot on the thumb cannot move, and those born at the joint of the thumb may be able to move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The incision on the fleshy one is easy, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide pair of scissors.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	So hold on tightly while cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with a hard knot at the shoulder, first you must cut around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then scrape it until it is clean.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The scabs that come on both toes together are caused by birthmarks or scars from wounds or burns or similar things.`
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you must cut that nail, so that the thumb returns to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two cloths or gauze soaked in rose oil so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Where you place between two pieces of thin lead until the spot is closed as it ought to be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If scabs come on any of his toes with the palm, cut off that adhesion as necessary;`
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The eyes are large veins enclosed and filled with melancholic impurities that come from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him sometimes a purge for the colon, and then treat it with the basilica remedy.`
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways to treat with iron:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One way is to cut them and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to tie off the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, raise the leg with hot water very strongly until the thick blood is thinned out, then hold the leg of the patient above the hip joint down to below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place or two or three with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the virtue of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then apply a poultice, and instruct him to bind himself with fresh meat around a black cloth.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, but this harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of him is done in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the patient's leg if there is much hair on it, then place him in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If you have no bath, heat him by the fire, and then make an incision on the vein near the long bone at the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with an awl and strip the vein from each side until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And when it is seen red and black, and enters the skin, it seems like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then place a hook underneath so that it lifts the vein from the skin, and gently strike it with an awl, then make another incision three fingers above;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape off the skin above the vein until it appears; then lift it at the root, as you have done before, and tie it to another sinew, as you did initially.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another incision, or several if necessary; then lift it and cut at the two ends of the foot; then draw it out and lift it up to the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull it out from incision to incision until it all comes out; then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then insert a needle with strong doubled thread, tie it, pull it out, place it under the root, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it does not break off, for if it breaks, you cannot pull it out or lift it, and this harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And once you have completely treated it, place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound's location
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him treat until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut all of it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the face is curved and does not cut straight, so that it does not cut into the vein
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and its curve should be large because if it were fine, it would cut into the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein enters the legs, in warm parts where no grass or tree grows, and on land where there is no moisture
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to rot that comes from under the skin, as when it enters the body like a serpent or worm, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there appears a very large inflammation on the leg, then the location changes, and the vein starts to protrude like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound opens, you should wrap around it a piece of linen measuring about one and a half spans up to two spans, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging on the leg; every time blood flows out at the front, you should wrap it around the linen and retie it
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut at its root, so that it is all exposed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will enter into the flesh, causing an abscess and decay in that place, and evil disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be treated bit by bit until its head, leaving nothing remaining on the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein, when treated from the length of two palms or three, and once a man came to me whose was four palms long; when you cut it, insert one finger into the hole, and pierce it until its bottom so that all comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter within be emptied, and apply medicines around it to prevent decay for several days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes there are many arrows in this vein, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and there are many holes from which blood flows;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it happens often to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel it well as it travels from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as come worms, serpents, flies, and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and its harmfulness is doubted because when it goes through the body and reaches the head, it comes to the eye by chance, enters it, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drawn out, one can only be sure that it is when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore you must tie the limb above and below with a strong and tight ligature, then cut into it and draw out the worm, and if the worm is buried deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize the spot with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it causes is that it damages the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming near the head by the eye, press down on it firmly with your eyebrow, then cut upwards, and pull out the feather;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And the patient should use cleansing of body with medicinal solvents to remove corrupt humors, and avoid consuming rotten foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	due to pain caused by windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land 'vakivir', and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to a woman who was ill, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, it rose up like a worm to her shoulder, quickly as anything, just like quicksilver moving from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain then left that spot and struck into her shoulder, and soon afterwards it spread throughout her body, so that it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she kept turning around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how she could move thus from limb to limb because I had never seen this disease behave in such a way."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had seen many times that there was great pain moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it like this in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had dry skin, with veins exposed, and thus this constraint of wind appeared;
