et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	But they do not experience this according to this reason in those who are dislocated, who have moist skin and concealed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain which we have spoken of, quickly place your hand above and below it, and then strike until that constrained wind leaves its place;
et cauterize le leu;	And cauterize the location;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you cannot see it with your eyes, then treat it with things that expel wind, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, and similar other remedies.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Sighs are various according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The varieties of them are such that there are those which have large points, small ones, hairy ones, and smooth ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And there are those with two edges, those with tongues, and those with fragments
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those that fall onto any limb do so in one of two ways
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or onto the main members, such as head, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls into any of these locations, the signs of death that I will tell you about hereafter become apparent to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must beware of extracting this arrow for afterwards many deaths occur in various ways
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this bad sign does not appear to you and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	The sign of the head when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone is when there is sudden faintness, twitching, swelling, redness in the eyes, inflammation of the tongue, spasm, loss of consciousness, vomiting bile
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps it lacks fire from the nose, or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it loses speech and voice
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And there flows from the wound moist white pus like pigeon's dung, and also burns the flesh like fire.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, then take care of it, and pull out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign that an arrow has struck the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like a pigeon, and dark blood is cut off, and coldness and cold sweat come on, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know for certain that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The signs of a sigh that has entered the lung are that foam comes forth from the wound, the throat swells up, the patient changes color and sighs loudly and asks for cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the lung, it is near the little ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	And there is great pain and sighing and sorrow.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	All the shoulders' members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if a sigh falls into the stomach, sometimes undigested food may emerge from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if a sigh falls into the abdomen and much wind rushes out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or for drawing out the sigh."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine flows out and there is fever, and the patient feels great pain,
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that wounds are deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"The other limbs such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary limbs, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and similar limbs are safe according to various conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When a sigh is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous (as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise),"
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at home to someone that an arrow fell or was shot in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and drew it out from beneath the ear's fat without any injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And at another game, an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye beneath the paper wadding, and the arrow was stuck fast; only its point could be reached facing the timber, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, all in light iron without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The operation was successful, and no bad accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian; it was an Arab arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut the barbs and carefully drew out the arrow, and the Christian was saved.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And drew an arrow from someone at home that had fallen into the belly, believing him to be dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then after thirty days had passed, it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the boil, drew it out, and burned it with fire, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a boil fall on someone's back, and the wound is healed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the boil remained inside, and did not change its natural position or cause harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man on whom a boil fell on his face and the wound was healed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained thus without causing great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I drew out a boil from the prince's son, which had fallen into his throat and was slightly inclined towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the boil was completely covered over.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had fallen three days earlier.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I cut into it with a very fine needle and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed on the wound plastered with digestive attractant, for that reason the wound did not swell up.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And then the tip of the arrow appeared
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster again the next day, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained like that for a long time until he felt the arrowhead inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	And he told me this
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive hot medicine to the wound for many days until it opened, and I tested it and felt that the tip of the arrow was protruding from its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I pushed into the opening of the wound with this hot medicine until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it took nearly four months for this to pass, and then the wound opened up so that I could insert pliers into it, but I moved them from side to side and could not pull out anything.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to devise and plan ways of instruments, until on the third day I found well-made forceps according to its final form described in this chapter, with which I grasped and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then closed it, and the wound was healed, and the patient became entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	But I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may place your treatment on what I did not mention, for books cannot cover everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But wise masters compare even small things, and find new works and new instruments according to the needs of the case at hand in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows come out of the limbs where they are stuck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the wound where they entered, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps out where it enters is an arrow entering flesh, and sometimes it happens suddenly.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out, leave it until the flesh can be pushed around, and let the wound heal.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it there for some days, and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then if it comes out, and if it does not come out, carefully pierce around it with a fine probe until the area around it is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at its head and goes as far as one of the brain's ventricles, some accidents that I mentioned may occur to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	So do not pull it out, but leave it alone for some days until it becomes even again, because if the arrow has reached the brainstem, death will result.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach too deep, and the patient remains for a few days without bad symptoms, then attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then administer poultices around it as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound until it's clean.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is buried in the flesh so that one cannot see it, then search for it carefully.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with some tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein involved, then cut until the wound is large enough.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that keep it in place, cut away the flesh that is stuck on both sides of the wound so that you can then break off or bend the barbs to extract the arrow.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be careful not to break the arrow, lest it cause greater injury when extracting it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then wait until the place around is properly prepared, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding is profuse and hinders you, then apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And guard yourself from incising nerves and veins; devise how you might carefully remove the arrow without danger, either swiftly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And place the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help. If you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where something of it is visible or the skin is swollen there, can be felt around
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then cut down until you can grasp it with forceps, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it is now stuck.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it for now and resume the extraction later until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	If the shaft of the arrow is there, push it all the way in.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if the shaft falls out and you see that there is no exit point, then administer a cauterizing instrument so that the tip of the arrow enters its hollow.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then apply fire, and if the arrowhead is stuck, insert an instrument with a pointed entrance end to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead has entered, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as it ought.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead falls in the thigh or abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is nearby, you can grasp it with forceps.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And beware not to grasp the vein or nerve, then extract it and sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	until healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat bones is similar to a bird's beak, and here is an illustration of that shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small ones, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, for driving into the point of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	Here is the shape of forceps for grasping and pulling:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which we bleed, among them 16 are in the head:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two temporal arteries behind the ears called "doubles 'herbechi'.
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And two arteries visible in both temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins in the inner canthus of each eye called "aspirantes";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	The vein that runs across the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein which is at the head of the nose
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two arteries that are in the neck
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins which are above the mouth's lips, and these are called 'augeherich'.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The five main veins in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the Cephalic vein, running along the right side of the chest, which common people call the 'vein of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the second is called 'fast', and is composed of the Cephalic and Basilic veins, which common people call the 'vein of the heart'.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the Basilic vein runs along the left side of the chest; common people call it 'the vein of the belly', and it lies above the forearm's muscle and is visible on the palm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the Salvatellite vein is the vein that runs between the little finger and ring finger, having two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The first is below the curve of the pouch on the left side, and the second starts which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein called 'nesse', which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The discharge from veins that are behind the ears helps with old ulcers and headaches;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the characteristics of the discharge are, as I tell you, to raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then have the patient turn their neck towards one side with a wry neck, until two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then seize them with your thumb and index finger where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein upstream, and cut both skin and vein deeply with two strokes, until you see blood flowing;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold it still and bind it until it heals.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for migraine, catarrh, and habitual ophthalmia, and for the flow of tears from the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the healer are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient holds his neck steady so that the two veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, and then compress gently.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then raise the heart above the vein with your middle finger and place the lancet below it, lift the vein upwards and cut it, as you have done with the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then unbind the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then bind it tightly and leave it until it heals.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their dislocation and extraction, where this book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the frontal vein is as valuable as the bleeding of the temporal vein for treating old facial diseases, and for migraine and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the veins appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called 'fosseur', of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein and press with your hand or something else until you see as much blood come out as you wish;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein so it stops bleeding, often with a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, do not let the bandages be too tight;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And tie it diagonally, because the bone is nearby and by chance the bandage may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in both eyelids helps with the eyes, and with redness, itching, inflammation of the eye, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the nature of their injury is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it to one side, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the wound appears, and it should be a cross-shaped cut, about two fingers long and wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are thin, they may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then wipe off the blood until you have enough, and then tie with cotton, tying it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	This wound from the vein near the nose is beneficial for fever, and madness with frenzy, and facial diseases such as migraines and redness that appears on the face, especially when it's chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the nature of this wound is that the patient strains their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, and takes the thin flame and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep, make it flow with blood according to your need, then let it rest one night, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The urine of two goats helps with constipation, and aids in mixing medicines, and is beneficial for many diseases, including epilepsy, erysipelas, corrosion, herpes, and skin diseases.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the properties of urine are such that the patient draws his neck under both [feet].
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master be standing at the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on a chair; then open a vein on the arm a little wide, then let blood temperately, as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then do the same on the other vein; then untie the bandage, and press around both veins moderately so that the patient does not faint.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave it until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of bodies
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"The juice of the veins of the lips above aids in coldness in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and nose and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of treatment are to make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip and look at two veins, one on the right lip and one on the left, which are known to be black, and have small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do likewise for the two veins that are above and below them, for they are of the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The treatment of the veins beneath the tongue helps after treating the cephalic vein, for it is used in strangulation of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the treatment are that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, lifts their tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore heal both [the dislocations] one after the other, but do not press too hard inward, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the elbow that are commonly treated are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Either by pressing with a broad flame, or with a fine olive oil drop like a cutting edge, which is called 'anesil';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the mirror blow is very well known, and is wide as you see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the hairy veins that are full of visible thick blood, and contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more pointed and fine, and is for letting the veins that have thin, lemon-colored blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cautery of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps those with illnesses in the throat, neck, chest, and belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the cauterizer to cauterize skillfully, and to beware of the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow abundantly, then it must be stanched, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be pointed but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the boil does not open visibly, then you must draw it out and replace it with another one
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or any vein from it, or you can also insert the vein into its place in the arm
elle apert manifestement;	it opens visibly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	Cut at the flame like a knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the place of the vein, then before extracting it, touch that place until you feel the pulse
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink and tie the arm, then cut the vein with the flame like a knife
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	but be careful not to injure the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery.
eschui la donques.	Avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see something sticking out like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Therefore, quickly place your finger firmly on top, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, for this happens many times:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Then bind the arm and leave it like that; do not move it.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful, do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	But if the bleeding does not stop and you faint, and a physician is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for its mouth draws back.
et estainche li sans.	And stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a fig bark, split it open, and take one half and bind it firmly until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the bleeding stops, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	But if not, then treat it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have said;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the bleeding is not harmful in many cases due to the small area of the wound and the power of binding the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein's blood vessel in the middle helps because it brings blood from above the head and below the body; for this reason, it is composed of both the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	The surgeon must beware of the nerve that lies beneath; if it is pierced too deeply and the nerve is struck, it will swell and cause injury to the veins, perhaps rendering healing impossible.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	This nerve is often exposed; however, if it is not exposed in some men due to its fineness, then you must heal it with the aid of an instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Avoid damaging the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise;"
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein from the head also aids in bringing blood from the head and helps with the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to cauterize with the olive-shaped flame or the myrtle-shaped flame, for this is the safest of all veins because there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Still, it is necessary to seek out the lightest position, and do not distress if the first attempt fails; begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the place swells for some men when they fail at the first attempt, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of letting depends on your judgment."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that health is maintained only to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are on the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely, the cephalic, basilic, and median cubital vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and winter after meals, when signs ofpletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	One should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but it should be done when needed, at any hour and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to circumcise children until they are fourteen years old, nor women during pregnancy except after four months have passed.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years of age receive this medicine.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be circumcised, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor should one circumcise someone who is too full of food, or drunk at that moment, nor someone suffering from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And one should not circumcise after an attack of the colic, vomiting, diarrhea, menstruation in women, hard labor, staying awake all night, fasting, or anything that weakens the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then thin out the humors if there is copious blood, through foods and drinks and medications, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter into the bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtilize the blood, and heal the vein of the leg around the third, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard on that day against labor, and overeating, and lust, and similar things
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be lying and joyful, and let the healthier person's arm be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm twice or thrice, then tie the bandage in the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the place with his hands until you feel the veins swell and can see them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then let the bledder wet the blade of a little old oil, then place his left thumb on that vein below where he wishes to cut, so that the vein does not slip or break when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that slip away like strings when bled, and some are so full of windiness that when the blade is placed upon them, it retreats with the blade, and cannot open the vein, such are they.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the surgeon to be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens at first, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, then try again a little lower or higher quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps abscesses will form;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter a bath, then resume the cauterization if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the hole is small, or blood flows thinly and you doubt that not much blood will come out, then apply fire directly to that hole;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And open it quickly before the place becomes swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound swollen, then do not recommence the cauterization, and place a little bit of oil ointment on it, for it lightens the body's blood, and in this case, the ointment that the oil brings is beneficial.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the ointment of oil in each cauterization that you perform on veins, to staunch the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	This same thing is done by thrice and bowels of urine when placed upon the wound.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If blood is too thick and does not spread out evenly.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess appears, which happens often, especially when there is no cauterization except for that one time when the vein opening is small, then you hurry and place on the wound a sponge moistened in water and heated slightly, and hold it there for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you must do this after the bleeding stops from the vein opening, and if it remains on the wound for several days any blackness or greenness will not harm it.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put on some aloë or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastich, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and swelling occur at the sinew of the basilisk:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Therefore place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft under hand pressure, then that is a bad swelling.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Hence do not apply anything of what we have mentioned, for it may cause the artery to break:
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off the blood according to each person's constitution and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red:
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it large, let it be until it is diminished;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and bloated, and needs bloodletting, make the incision larger, and let the flame be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to one who is weak, do the opposite; he must be warmed often with warm poultices, and they should be applied by cutting, not pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of warming prevents bleeding and damage to nerves, and it is better than warm poultices that are long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body fails with warmth, give him pounded bread in juice of pomegranates;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if he is overheated, then bleed him three or four times; And if he has a cold constitution, let him eat before the warming bread pounded in thick syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they faint during bloodletting, after losing much blood, then they must inhale broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have spoken of in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to evacuate one arm and have bloodletting done again afterward, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he be bled a little at a time according to his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to evacuate one arm after the first bloodletting and has a strong body should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have bloodletting done on another part of the body should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood inside the body that is already heated, which causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	So one must draw off a large quantity and widen the opening as much as possible without causing pain;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	After you have prepared all the necessary conditions for healing, and you place your hand on the swollen area when it is hot, ensure that death does not take the place of improvement, which happens many times if the healer is careless.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not necessary for you to see blood flow out a second time and close the hole by pressing strongly upon it when you untie the arm.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	Nor if it is crooked, should he hastily extend his arm, for that would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But let him remain until the swelling comes down a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And where you apply the tip of the flame, keep it there until the blood that has frozen at the mouth of the vein flows out; then place some thread moistened in water and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	"But if the vein is swollen, do not let go nor squeeze too hard until the inflammation has subsided."
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	"And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, do so either in the same vein or in another one, or even in the other arm."
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	"The vein in the arm is opened in place of the vein in the head because it is more accessible."
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is for the patient to immerse their hand in warm water until the bones feel hot;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it gently so that the vein appears well; then treat the swelling from the side, not from the length or width;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the wound be wide, and let it be cut close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, then place the hand in warm water, and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is inflamed, then do not place the hand in warm water, for one puts it there more often in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the cut of this vein is safer than all other veins, as neither artery nor nerve runs through it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The incision for saving the hand on the right side has value for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and place it in warm water until the vein becomes swollen and visible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if you cut across the vein, and remove all of it completely, then nothing will be harmed;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	But do not cut too deep, for nerves lie beneath all flesh; then place the hand in warm water if blood is congealed in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And when you have drawn enough blood, apply oil and a little salt to quickly cauterize the wound, and do this for each cut."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The bleeding of the vein in the left hand is beneficial for those suffering from mumps, and it should be done in the same way as I have described for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The juice of the soapwort is beneficial for all illnesses below the body, such as those of the womb, retention of fluids, and diseases of the spine, thighs, and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient places their foot in warm water and rubs along the vein until it disappears, then ties above the ankle joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and there are many sinews going up from the foot above it;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Therefore cauterize where the largest sinew or tendon is located, or at the ankle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you cauterize above the foot, beware of the nerves that are below it and cut across like cutting meat;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, immerse the foot in water again and allow the vein to empty completely."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If the cauterization fails the first time, then repeat it slightly higher the second time because the place is burned;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise to the sore on the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is on the outside ankle, and bleeding it is beneficial for lower back pain when caused by hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his cauterization is such that the patient enters into a bath and holds four fingers above the ankle while twisting, otherwise the vein will not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, then drain all of it in every way you can, including across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it out, for the place is dry and it responds much to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, drain any vein of hers that opens towards the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and draw out as much blood as you see, then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and bind it tightly;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now drained.
des sainies de ventouse	And regarding the applications of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made from horns, or earthenware, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that is done without striking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cupping done by striking and bloodletting is performed at fourteen locations on the body, one of which is directly on top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the other is within the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And the other is on either side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup beneath each shoulder;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and suction cups on either arm;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And suction cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	Suction does not draw blood, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, unlike venesection;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be applied in any disease caused bypletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to apply suction cups due to illness or habit, we will do so every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and at all times.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to apply suction cups, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And those who findpletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness before the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an swollen tongue, and vomit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are also those who dream, and see by nut's blood, and wounded, dead, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially during the month, we will order them to be leeched three hours after noon."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sweat of the muses helps against headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this happen after evacuation of all blood;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventosation is in place of the sweat of the head, and those who are cold by nature or have catarrh should not use it, for it harms them greatly;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore old men should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful. Therefore, the leech should be placed a little lower to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And ventosation on the neck is instead of sweat from the head and basilisk, and it helps with constriction of the chest, and breaking of the channel of the lung, and coughing, and repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And then a little pressure is needed, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause harm to the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The winds of the second rib on the neck are useful for headaches and inflammation of the eyes, migraine, strangling, pain in the roots of the teeth.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the surgeon that he expresses his hand during setting so that he does not cut the artery and cause blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The winds under the chin are useful for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar mouth ailments.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is in place of the treatments for the second lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"The shoulder windings are good for diseases that come from heat and swelling."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The winds on the sides are as useful as the three veins of the arm, for they attract blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the surgeon not to go too deep with the cautery, for the place is bare of flesh and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttocks is useful for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for illnesses below, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large, and made of brass, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps if it were too thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs are applied openly because they draw blood from the whole body and are useful for old pains in the loins, sciatica, and the bladder; and they reduce swellings.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are placed on the two hips and the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after prolonged use and cause coughing in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the cupping glass is to place it first empty and suck gently, then quickly place it and move it evenly, without stopping until you see the area redden and swell, and the redness of blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then burn, and reset the cupping glasses, and beware of the condition of the body, for there are many who have tender flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to strike only once, and one must make wide, somewhat deep wounds;
et suce legierement.	And suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, then strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, then strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to draw out only a little blood at a time, one strike suffices.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish much blood, then strike frequently;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, strike deep, and make the incisions so that the heart is pierced suddenly; this is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and narrow pores, you should oil the cups' openings with aperient and dissolvent oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is inflamed, with oil of violets, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of melons;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in the ear, with oil of watercress, or lilies, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excessiveness is thick and cold, use almond oil or balm oil or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if it is for one who has tender flesh and wide pores, then no oil should be put on, but it should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of morelle, or water of cucurbit, or water of porcellain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should rise using this method: with myrtle water or sumac water and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive sweating should rise from old wine, or water of buckthorn, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And one should not use cupping glasses before the bath nor during it, but after the bath one or two hours.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after cupping; one must warm oneself when being cupped and when finished with cupping.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the person being treated is choleric, and if their blood is too thick and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	Then they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with garlic, and similar foods.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And minced pigeons, and castrated goat meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with cold constitution should take syrup of honey and mid-level perfumed wine that is between old and new, and minced apples, minced pigeons and small birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day when he expects to vomit, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men sometimes three times or musk before vomiting, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Let the blood be subtly taken, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are placed without striking are those placed on the liver, and on the side, and on podagry, and on the stomach, cheek, back and thigh; for these members do not suffer to be struck upon, and they only do it to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when there is an inflamed breast.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the dampness from the limb, as we place cupping glasses on the stomach and head to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves pain when there is congestion or stone, so it may by its attractive power perhaps remove the congestion, or dislodge the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And similarly it does when placed upon the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy, in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let there be two of them with a width of half a palm and depth of one, having on the side around the middle a small hole like that for putting in a needle, made of brass, so that it does not cut the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And he should have in the middle a rod of iron or bronze for placing an enclosed candle upon it, and they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the cups used on children differ from those used on adults, and for thin people differ from those used on fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cup upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Light the candle wick or the linen and place it in the cup through the rod that is inside the cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup so as not to burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it upon the limb, and ensure that the hole we spoke of is positioned upwards so that when one wants to, steam can escape and the cup can be removed;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And again light the linen wick as before, and repeat this process often if necessary.
