En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Thus the cup used in cases of pleurisy with acute fever has no rod or hole and is only heated when it is full of water; it is placed upon the limb alone;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the formula:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not applied except in limbs where you cannot apply cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in fleshless places, like the toes or nose, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of using them are that when you find leeches in clear, sweet waters without any defect, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they are hungry and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then let the vein and the cupping glass be sanctified, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and fall off, if it's a place where you can apply a cupping glass, then do so, for this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the limb gently and then with water, very carefully, and then squeeze it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the wound is too close to the body of the patient, then soak the linen bandage in cold water and place it on top until the blood thins out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the blood is multiplied, then apply powdered vitriol or saltpetre and similar substances until it thins out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you may place half a handful of peeled peas on the wound, leaving them there until they absorb at the site; this will now stop the bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if more are needed, take others from the patient.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the wounds will not close, then rub fresh blood on the wound and insert a needle until it bleeds; then apply the linen bandage, and as soon as it feels the blood, it will absorb.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are full, then powder a little aloe and celandine or ash on them; they will now congeal.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is very necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the treatment of fractures and dislocations."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians ignore this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is extracted from our land, as I found none of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I know nothing of it, except through the science of ancient books which I have studied so much that I have practiced this science, and through experience, and through habit in my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are arranged, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the contents of the words and chapters where wise men place their understanding and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any breaking or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs to someone, you must quickly examine the patient on both sides, unless there is something preventing it entirely, such as weakness of body, or a child, or an old person.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid eating cold foods, such as cold meats, and the flesh of birds and hares, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not overeat on foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are uncertain about a hot abscess or an expansion of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his first government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with foods that cause good growth and are moistening, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, apples, cow's milk, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment muscles grow back more quickly and the fracture heals faster;"
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot be well reset or mended according to their nature due to weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But if there is no remedy, bind the broken bone with strong bandages that will hold and join the limb together until it heals as before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not expose all the points of his work, and therefore he must be fed on hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"There are fractures that occur suddenly, like falling from a horse, and others that occur gradually, like the splitting of a feather for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with only a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory recalls in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the bone is broken when the joint is twisted and opens wide upon being pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist nor sound upon touching it, and the patient feels little pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But he can also have torsion, or splitting, or slight fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move him by hand, but apply the medicines that come later and then gently immobilize him."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fractures which go inwards and have two parts separated must be aligned evenly before an abscess forms there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess does form there, let it remain some days until the abscess is subdued;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then set it evenly at the movement you can do lightly and bloodlessly, for know that the restoration of this one is easier than those with fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then bind it as is necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone has broken into pieces, then extend it with two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or use your hand for small limbs, or use two bands, or one band and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And align the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are dislocated, you reset them with all your strength, putting the fragments back in their places gently, and ensure that through your work the patient suffers no injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And join together closely the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel carefully with your hand whether it seems well joined or not:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If you reset it beautifully, and do not pull too hard or press as those who cause heat and constriction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And once the limb is set, instruct the patient not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the limb is secured so that the patient feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if it causes any pain, then it has not been set properly, and you must place it in such a position that there is no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And ensure that it is set correctly, so that there are no twists when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	The condition of the broken limb will be according to what I tell you
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that fractured limbs are diverse in size, length and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	It is necessary to wrap soft and fine linen cloths around (it).
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are thick, like thigh and calf:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	It is necessary to wrap it in a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage encircles the entire limb evenly and holds it tightly without any gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then wrap it with light bandages, three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on all the bandages. Then go up above the fracture and tighten less so that the fracture can separate a little from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the bandage bit by bit until you grasp a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it around again on the fractured area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture and tighten it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the ligaments wads of linen or cloth until it is entirely even; then bind everything above with gauze, and then place well-made compresses on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place on top something that cools the hot abscess and reduces swelling; leave it like this for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then press down on your compresses with something half the width of a wide reed or a piece of wood used for hoes or palm ribs, shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But the compress placed on the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or length.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then press down on the compresses just as you did in the first layer; then tie it securely with string, just as you did in the first layer over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	Narrower above, always less
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And the threads should be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of some fools who make their bindings from twisted linen cords, which is a great error; for the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' breadth between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	"And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the bandaging on healthy areas, place linen bandages or wool wadding underneath them so that it does not bruise."
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	"When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the skin is broken, I will speak about its treatment later on."
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	"And know that one should not bind all broken limbs with splints on the first day."
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it does not need to have stitches put in until after five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of a hot swelling appearing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the manner of ancient poultices for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill and mix it with plenty of eggs; and this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, use it for a poultice to restore fractures in many ways, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method for applying plasters that restore breaks, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take acacia leaves, dill, wild celery, opobalsamum, gum arabic, and mastic; mix them together.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Add myrrh and aloewood; mix them together.
alechil VIIII З.;	Grind aloe vera roots into a fine powder (7 parts).
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And grind it into a fine powder, mixing it with beaten egg yolk.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's complexion is hot, this plaster should be used as it has good properties and quickly heals broken bones. It benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method for applying a plaster that treats sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mastic and balsam of Peru; mix them together (10 parts).
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Add myrrh and aloewood; mix them together (9 parts).
acaice VI З.;	Acaia six (6) parts.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Bole armoniac ten (10) parts, grind well, and knead with honey or beaten egg yolk; apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat dislocations and bones out of their places, alleviates pain occurring, and reduces swelling and breaking:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, moisten it with hot water and oil cooked together, then place on the location.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating heat from an abscess, and removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to treat that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and common mallow leaves, grind them together and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner to plaster for the healing of bone fracture and to soften the remainder of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take equal parts of marsh mallows, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, and wheat flour;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind the mixture together and cook it with wine. If the limb is inflamed, cook it with moistened coriander water or water, and apply it as a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner to plaster stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess forms on the healing member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take equal parts of marsh mallow root, flaxseed, balm, meadowsweet, savin, violet flowers, and chamomile flowers;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	"Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more. He says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard."
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	"And it seems to Galen that one should put dry and slightly warm things on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar substances, as we have said."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Other plaster method that is good for injury and pain
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and chopped comfrey leaves, or chicken feathers, and figs, and equal parts salt, grind them, and make a plaster with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove it after a little while, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not, leave it on for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry up and remove it, and take off the plaster immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and damp sea sponge, dip it in water, and apply it to the place until the itching stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool wadding moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it on with a bandage until you are sure of having a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and may the pain be removed, then begin again the subtle massage, with a little plaster, but do not pull too hard as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen are all gone, and you need plaster and bandages again, then resume it, just as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	If there is no improvement in the limb from what we have said, then do not remove the plaster until three or four or five or seven days have passed;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes leave it on for 20 days, according to what is seen, until the fracture becomes apparent and the flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then tighten more than before, and let his flesh grow thick, as I said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the wound drying out too much, know that there can be no healing from it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore apply warm water compresses each time you remove the plaster, every third day, and relax a little with massage;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Thus through this treatment, healing comes quickly to the limb, and correct immediately those foolish doctors who reset limbs incorrectly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is harmful, and it involves fearful operations, and I see nothing else but doubt and performing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of fractures, with diverse appearances, and their causes are distinguished;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by blows from swords that break the collarbone all the way down to its attachment beneath the bone, like an axe or a tree trunk;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And thus this kind of fracture is called "hachet" (axed).
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or when the sword cuts across the bone without piercing it, this type of fracture is called 'absolute'
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And both these two types of fractures result in large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion that embeds, splits, or crushes from a fall onto stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the bone tissue beneath the bone or is above it, and this wound can be large or small
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	Also there is a fracture where the wound is thin and subtle like a hair, with a small crack; this type of fracture is called 'capillary'.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by being struck with a stone or by falling, or by something similar, causing a fragment of bone to enter inwards, and the site becomes elevated like the bottom of a cauldron;
si entre li piere dedens.	If between the stones within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and occurs with all kinds of fractures where small pieces are dislocated like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the displacement on them, by careful inspection, and by the corrupted flesh that is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, pay attention to any accidents of illness, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever with chills, inflammation of the eyes, etc., in many conditions, he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accident and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, especially in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you should hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut open the broken part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And take the patient's head gently and uncover the bone in all possible ways, carefully exposing the wound's appearance; if blood or pus flows while uncovering the bone, clean it with what is necessary, and fill the place with bandages moistened in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the pus is calmed, and ensure that there is no more bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to remove around the bone, which is done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is thus: You shall cut narrowly before at the tip of the head; this is the shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I add another cut, greater than the first one."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And another manner is thus: You should have many diverse cuts, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of steel.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and perform them lightly so that you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and sturdy, then you must first bore around it before administering cuts with tartaric mixture, not too deep that they pierce through the soft bone, and the point should have a margin or circle above it to prevent the point from passing beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have many such points so that each fits properly on the edge of the bone, so that you may have tartaric mixture for all wounds.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of applying tartaric mixture:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities for boring around a broken bone are that you place the tartaric mixture on the bone and turn with both hands until you know the bone is bored.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then reposition the cautery elsewhere a little later, and do so all around. Then cut with incising tools the space of bone that is between the pores, and do this more finely than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you pull out the bone by hand, or with any of the instruments you have such as forceps.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and ensure that you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and pulled out the bone, then you must reset the remainder of the bone with another tool resembling an incising tool, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incising tools;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then heal the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of working is that which Galien describes, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And strike it very strongly, this is his saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone where the fracture appears more openly, so that when you have exposed this part, then place beneath the head of this lenticular knife, of which here is the form:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side alone, and if the part is acute on both sides, then the cutting will be towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike gently with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and beware of the tissue beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, scrape it gently, for one can scrape well without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the dura mater, and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces, then it is necessary to remove this prominence and remove the scales with a fine razor that you should have in various quantities, so as to accommodate each place according to the operation and shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"So remove first with large razors, and then with more delicate ones, and do not stop doing this until it is completely done."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other haircuts and subtle breaks, you must direct the cause according to its alignment;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, you must take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you can, so as not to strain the sinews, then apply one bandage above and another below, but do not draw it too tightly that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it thus for one or two days until the boil is softened, then untie it and apply medications such as iris roots, almond flour, incense powder, and aristologia, and similar substances;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And grind these substances into a powder, sprinkle it on the wound, and apply healing ointments without causing pain.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is always clean, so that no ointment remains on it nor does any bowels gather there, for when bowels gather on the brain cloth they will rot and cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when something irritating is placed on the sinews, it causes them to wither.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"Therefore be careful, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness comes upon it due to the medication applied, which has this virtue, then you should take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix them together in a cloth, and apply it to the sinews;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after explaining ways of treatments, make sure he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or just one by itself, for they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And the one below is made of cartilage and does not break, unless it gets hit hard or twisted, but then it will heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should place your little finger in the hole of the nose and align this break with your index finger on the outside, until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	"And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must insert a small rod with a rounded end into it."
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if both parts are broken, then do likewise, and try to restore it on the first day if possible;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	Otherwise, after seven or ten days, when the swelling has subsided, then apply bandages made of linen cloth to the top of the nose if it's broken on one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	When you bend one towards another side, if there is a fracture there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers said that one must grease the tents with butter, changing each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is correct, but it is necessary that they be moistened in a mixture of almond oil and powdered myrrh;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bandage on until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	Sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of bandages, and if the fracture stays in place, then the patient feels better.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or faire le ciel que vous voyez
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	"And if inflammation appears in the nose while you are working on it, then insert there wax or cotton soaked in rose oil or a little bit of diacynthion."
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not form, then apply a plaster made from flour of sesame and powdered frankincense mixed with almond oil, followed by light dressings, without binding the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small and broken into many pieces, remove them with appropriate tools, then stitch the split and treat it with things that involve skin and wound-healing, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside it, then treat it with hot water compresses, placing lead plates until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only on one side, not completely broken into two pieces, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary that, if the fracture is on the right side, you place your two index fingers in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left jawbone, place your right hand's two index fingers in the mouth, gently push the fracture with them, and align it using your other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced by two fingers' width, you must apply traction forcefully until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there is movement or loosening of teeth, constrain them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply wax to the broken jawbone and cover it with a doubled cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a well-made splint or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, tying it at the point where you can. Instruct the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure has changed, untie it on the third day, then put back what was dislocated.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a poultice made of flour ground with abundant eggs or sesame flour after removing the cauterization.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a light linen cloth over the poultice, and if the poultice dries out but the patient's condition does not improve, leave it until it is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both fracture and wound together, make sure no fragment of bone has been removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so that the fracture can be properly treated with appropriate tools.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it with a cautery according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and place one of the bandages suitable for this, to encourage flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	From the scalpel
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	A broken collarbone happens frequently near the shoulder, and fractures occur in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	either it is broken and dislocated at two places with fragments, which is the easiest to reset;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is thus when there is no wound; you should have two assistants so that one can hold the dislocated limb steady.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then align the fracture with your two hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round spear of cloth or wool, and it should be thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the limb, holding the spear with your hand so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the blade of the scalpel forward because it has gone in deep, then have the patient lie on their side with a pillow under their shoulder and place a small cushion underneath. Then have your assistant press down on the shoulder so that the bone of the blade is lifted up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then adjust the fracture with your two hands, and if you find it displaced, then you must cut.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull the fragments gently apart, and if the bone cannot join due to some obstruction, then cut with one of the incissors you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	But you shall place beneath the forceps this instrument, to guard against dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	And it should resemble a spoon, not pointed, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it should have two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the outline of the wound you made when you reduced the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of hot swelling, then close the wound, and if the outline is small, or you doubt hot swelling, cover the wound with rags and towels according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if granulation tissue is not present, soak a piece of gauze in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The reduction of bone without wounds or cuts is to place on the bone a plaster made of powdered millstone and egg white, then place light dressings on it, and place a splint under the ankle if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage, about a palm's width, then place a double cloth over the dressings and plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a fine iron rod three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the rod on the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the sound shoulder, and under the dislocated shoulder;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And tighten each part, and when you see that the sling holds the break in place, and you clearly see that the rod does not move on the broken bone, then wrap it every day, and when the ligatures relax, then secure it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow under the dislocated shoulder while they sleep to raise it up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	So that the break is eased by the lightening of the shoulder, where you bind the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except in case of misfortune, for up to twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then restart the emplacement if you see it is necessary, and hold it firmly until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it will be restored in 28 days at most, and sooner for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Treatment of shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It sometimes happens that the shoulder joint is broken or dislocated, and cannot be put back into place without touching it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the dislocation appears according to the shape of the break, then reset it according to its natural form in every possible way;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then place on the joint powder of the millstone with abundant egg whites, light bandages, and a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place a wide and thin strip of cloth over it, slightly larger than the shoulder; if there are any hairs underneath the cloth near the shoulder joint, pack those hairs with linen bandages so that the cloth lies evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it firmly with a large bandage so that the strip of cloth does not move from its place; check the binding every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it dislocates, hold it tightly, and place the bone evenly if it is out of its proper position; then let the patient lie on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this period is completed, release it, but be sure, for bone does not move out of place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone sticks out and is not beneath the heart, cut it off and apply the treatment for fracture of the collarbone as mentioned earlier to encourage granulation tissue formation.
de la brisure dou pis	Treatment of elbow fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The limb may sometimes break in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks near the joint.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, it tilts downward, and the patient feels great pain and faintness, and quickly, and sometimes vomits blood, and the marrow appears through the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the treatment is that the patient lies frequently on their back, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders together, and brings the ribs of both sides close to each other with your hands, carefully aligning them in all ways possible so that the bone appears as it should.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then place compresses and bandages on the broken bone with salt or other light dust, wrap it in a cloth, and secure it to the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And wind the bandage roundly to the back, and tighten it afterwards, and check each hour to see if it has loosened, and if it has, then tighten.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it is necessary to untie it, due to corrosion or itching that arises at the location, or pain or an abscess, then hurry and untie it, clean the area, and apply remedies as needed.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the area, and tighten it until it is firm.
de la brisure des costes	de la brisure des costes
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that fractures of the ribs occur only in large places after the back and at the top within, and they bend only because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one feels it well upon investigation, as you should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you align the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint, and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture leans inward, the patient feels great pain and pressure, similar to pleurisy, as the bone pokes the lung.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if it is sharp-pointed, and always present, vomiting much blood, it is serious, and the ancients considered it important.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should give him foods that swell the belly, to push back the break from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest abscesses come if they were not there before.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are there, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said that one puts cupping glasses on the spot to suck strongly, and this is similar to reason.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt whether the cupping glasses will draw out the excesses to the location due to weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And they said that one should cover the spot with moistened wool in hot oil, and then place tents between the ribs to make the belt equal, after which it should be treated with pleurisy treatment, flesh, and medicine."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone pressing on the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the location of the broken rib, and place something underneath the instrument to protect the spleen.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it is clean.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a boil that has been present comes, then put moistened cloths in rose oil on the location.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the location of this with what is suitable for an abscess, and keep it constantly warm on the side where it should be until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	"de la brisure dou col"
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is bone fracture in the neck, and rarely does it bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his hands are softened and swollen and numb, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that many are mortal in several conditions, and if he moves them and feels it well when they are pressed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if properly treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, take care if the feet are soft, and if there are accidents in the hands, and windiness and excretion happen involuntarily on the back.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it has been supported on its belly, excretion happens without control
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to saddle himself up, he cannot do so.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that they are deadly
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	"And if this accident does not happen to them, then the matter is lighter."
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if there is a hot boil, apply rose oil or goose fat oil to it until it is soothed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying emplastes, and the glue of a louse, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that part where they feel pain until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone dislocates, then you must cover on the chest.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together both lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then treat it with ointment, cleansing the flesh until it is healthy.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone head is broken, which is called 'the cow's head,' then place your left hand pouch and make it even with the other hand at your power, then set the splint and the pin, if you need them.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, then cut into it and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here is the translation for "de la brisure de l’os de la hainche":
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes it happens that the thighbone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a little bit of reduction to the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and cut from long ago, and decline toward the parting, and it comes to the patient pain in that place, and piercing, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the reduction is to stretch your hand upwards until you are above the dislocation;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know where the dislocation is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the dislocation is only at the head, then align this dislocation until it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or declines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of this break can be seen more easily.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And once you've aligned it, place your elbow on the emplacement, then place a wooden or bone splint over it, and hold the dislocation steady so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and press down on the spot below the ribs until the joint is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their sound side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess appears, do not touch it until the hot abscess has subsided, and then apply what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	then return to the reduction, and hold it in place as needed, if there is no bad outcome;
et c’est li maniere.	And this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the break of the shoulder blade
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the upper arm and the head of the shoulder blade, and if it is dislocated, it should be reduced according to one of these two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From which one is that you take a branch full of large muskroot, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie two branches with two cords, hang them up high, and have the patient sit upon the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then let him throw his broken arm upon the branch until it reaches the elbow and is held in place by a fork of wood, then weigh it down with some heavy object or have the assistant pull it downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then the physician should set the break even with his own hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to place the patient on their backrest and have them put their hand on their neck, then command two assistants to each take one end of the break with their hands—the first one taking the top part and the second one taking the bottom—and extend each one towards its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then hold down the lien below the break and above it, extending each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must place one cord in the middle under the elbow and the other towards the side, under the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And likewise if the break is towards the side, one must place the cord gently, without effort, so that the break is even in its place and on the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the fracture evenly as it ought to be, and bind it if no heat comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if heat does come, do not bind it for seven days, and apply a warm, moist cloth with rose oil until the swelling is reduced.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then bind it, and the way to bind it is thus: place the splint on the fracture, then bring the arm close to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And wrap it, binding tightly to the shoulder and arm so that the arm is in its proper place if nothing prevents it or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone has moved, use splints, and place a wider and stronger one on the fracture with two spaces between each splint, and make each splint large enough to extend three finger-widths beyond the fracture on either side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then press upon the elbow joints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, stronger but not pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the socket of the elbow joints, and their tightening, as we have said, when you reset the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it lie for seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then check every three days during the bandage, that no itching or swelling comes to the place where the limb cannot receive nourishment because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place beneath the shoulder blade one cushion full of even wool, and watch every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move or that the bandages do not soften;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If the patient is treated by medical means, and given the food that we have mentioned above, then the food should be made very subtle at first.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, then it should be made coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	It is customary that the arm and leg should be reset after 40 days in total;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	then one must untie it, apply baths and ointment medicines to set the joint straight.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the restriction is ugly and swollen, then delay untying it for forty days or two months.
