de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, called the two "fusciles," one of which is small and that supports the wrist;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and that is below, towards the little toe;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Sometimes only the large "fuscile" breaks, or sometimes only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bone is broken, restoration is easy and healing is quick;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	but when the large one is broken, healing is bad and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's the large dislocated joint, then it must be pulled back stronger;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	And stretch it over the cushion, and hold your hand pouch higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient lie across themselves, and put the cushion in front of them higher up, so that the patient does not suffer any strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend your arms below his hand or elbow, and another minister above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then the physician should place it even according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are broken fragments in the fracture, then each should be placed back in its proper position; and if any fragment is too short to grasp with forceps, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have mentioned before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is also wound breaking, I have spoken about that in the specific chapter;
si pren la cure.	So take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses appear, then take a bandage made of wax and rose oil that is neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind the bandage gently over it until the hot abscess is eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and apply the plaster of mill powder with an abundance of egg whites, then place the splints, and make the splint for the broken bone stronger and a bit wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And know that he must have six supports on his arm in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	Whether the break is in one bone or two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And bind more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, and all day long lessen when aligning, as I said at the beginning of this chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or harsh;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the lien after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must bathe the limb with warm water until this itch is soothed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the bandaging, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	"And if it is observed that the bandaging cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it thus for several days until the inflammation arrives, and then apply restraint."
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, then do not untie him for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if he extends his arms around him, then let him place his hands on his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and dislocation, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this dislocation can be restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and sometimes even in twenty, according to the mixtures and constitutions of the humours.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and around both wrists, there are few fractures; it is mostly dislocation that occurs.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the fingers of the hand are broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to sit crossed-legged and face straight ahead equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then he places his hand on a flat surface, and the ministers extend the broken bones, aligning them correctly until they are well-joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And applies the plaster and bandages if no abscess forms, then places a splint according to the size of the area.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the dislocation is around the wrist, then make a splint of cloth and tell the patient to bind it to their broken wrist.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And then bind it with a long bandage, and the splint should be as wide as the hand's length, binding it securely as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the fracture is on the back of the hand, then you must place a splint above it and another below in the palm so that the hand is open and straight. Then bind it all around the hand, and make sure the binding between both wrists is secure."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if any break comes to us from the hand, whether it's dislocated, set it right as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and secure it with a splint, and if you see fit, place a small upright stick to lift the dislocation, but do not move it;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the dislocation is in another finger, such as the index or one of the others, set it right and bind it with the healthy finger next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you can bind them all together at once, whichever works best, or place a splint on top, as in the case of dislocation.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And be careful with the restoration and placement of hot poultices, and protect those who are injured by it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Regarding the fractured hip:
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thighbone is often broken; you can see this when the hip turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And its restoration is accomplished by binding it above the break on one side and below it on the other.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each servant extends his cloth to his respective side evenly;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the dislocation is near the root of the thigh, then let one ligament be toward the knife handle, and the other ligament beneath the dislocation.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then the cloth should be placed by the knee, and the extension should be towards the foot;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then the physician places the bone evenly with both hands so that it is in its natural position, and then applies the splint, and the bandage, if any inflammation has come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an inflamed abscess, leave it to cool down before returning to your work and treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with two or three layers of hard bandage doubled over it, and fold back the excesses, then rotate the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and place a long thread between the hip and the leg, under the knee, and bring the ends of the thread upwards;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn up the bandage on the leg and thigh, then place the splints on the break, and place one splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the empty space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth strips to hold it evenly in place, then begin binding it tightly with three or four turns around the break;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher up on the break, make it less tight.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take two threads that you placed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above them, then return to the bottom of the thread so that you come close to the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And bind it tightly so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, until neither inflammation nor swelling nor anything similar occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if any such thing occurs, then untie it and dress whatever has happened, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that stick out, they must be cut off if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if one cannot, then one must split the joint open and draw forth fire;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And perform the treatment as we have said until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip is broken thus when one puts splints there, such as on the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, the patient does not limp from this restoration made in this manner.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is restored in about one month or a little less or a little more, depending on the differences in complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know this: In the cruciate ligament of the knee there is little breakage, but it tears often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is merely a crack or hole, and this happens with every wound, even without one. Everyone feels this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one places it evenly on what is round at its two ends so that they are assembled and can move;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then place the splint, and put a round splint there if necessary, and fasten it properly; then review all the arrangements that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply to each injury what is necessary until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is correctly called "mastella" and the other is called "ossicle";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And such breaking occurs equally in the leg, and therefore its restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all one. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely in every way.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, the foot turns inward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible;
et torne desoz.	and twists below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then provide extension, place it evenly, and tie the splints evenly
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, then take two strips of bark from a tree that will encircle the leg on both sides and be as long as the leg from the knee downwards
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	and wrap two bandages over and under them, tying it in the middle so that the leg cannot incline to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And some apply splints of long poplar wood to the leg, and if it is made of wood, they place the leg to prevent movement, and this is properly done in fractures where there is wounding.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each day the leg, to see if there's heat or other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the cure, then it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not suffer fractures, but sometimes bones in the foot are broken and so are the toes; and there are many ways of treating these injuries.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a bone fracture in the foot, and you see these bones protruding over one another, then place this patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then place your foot on theirs where the bones are sticking out, and press down until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then place the splint and bandages on it, put a small table with two legs under the foot's belly, then bind the foot tightly, then wrap cloth strips around it, and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any broken bones in the legs, restore them, just like we said for the hands.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place on both breaks a bandage according to the length of the leg, and let it be a bit wider, then place underneath the foot that table which I have mentioned, and hold it firmly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three breaks, or more, then place on each leg a bandage according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the table underneath the foot firmly.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And let it be so that when placed on top of the table, it touches the sole of the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I have mentioned for other breaks.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And treat each case as it deserves.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the thumb bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a pregnant woman is broken, have her sit upright, then lean her towards the back part, and let her be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the womb of the pregnant woman with cotton, and insert as much as one fist.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then push down the woman, little by little lift up the back, and then the shoulder joint pops out until it reaches the entrance of the socket, and the bone returns with the socket.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, then remove the shoulder joint, and after she has done so, reset it; do this for seven days or thereabout.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If the bone is restored, then take a lamb's bladder and tie a tube to its opening, insert the entire bladder into the socket.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the tube vigorously until the bladder fills up inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The joint will then return to its place.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for a few days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the hand or foot of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have described for the thighbone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these nearby fractures are not hidden from those who study and practice this art, and may they understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	Because fracture indicates in many cases the right path to restoration:
enten le donques.	Then do it accordingly.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	When the penis is broken, take a goose's neck and insert it into the penis;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap it with bandages around, and leave it on for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for anyone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the arm or similar, to be healed now, according to the treatments that we have mentioned.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then rinse it with vinegar or nitre, and begin to restore the fracture at that same hour or day, provided that no fever ensues.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a fever ensues, then delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the inflammation is calmed, and do not attempt to touch it on the third or fourth day, lest you cause further harm.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed above the heart, then it is necessary for you to put it back in place quickly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not align with your hands for even pressure, then use this iron tool that is seven or eight inches long, and its width should be according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and therefore it is necessary for the physician to mark three or four points on it, according to what is needed in each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your operation, and it should be pointed at the front and thicker towards the middle; thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palm" because the curved head must be placed on the exposed end of the bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And reset it once until it returns to its original position, with both sides evenly aligned.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is small and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as a knife or saw, to your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then scrape off what remains on the bone's surface and remove its small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If it is in place then moist a cloth in black vinegar and wipe it clean if it was inflamed;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	And do not apply any grease or other oily substance to the wound lest it cause decay and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then apply bandages once the bone has been reset, leave the wound uncovered, and cut the bandage all around according to the size of the wound, ensuring that the wound is not constricted by the dressing.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many foolish doctors have done this, causing harm or death to the patient at times;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the bandaging be softer and gentler than other bindings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad outcome will occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the location, do not put on bandages.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	Instead, wrap it with hard cloths, and tie them in place.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when after one or two days you see that the wound has begun to close, then remove what you have placed on it from all sides, and put on healing salve, such as tetrafarmacon salve and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	"And it is necessary that you wash the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is clean and healthy."
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	"And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the bowel moves down easily."
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	"And if many days pass and it does not heal but the bowel returns again, know that there are small bone fragments, so you must clean the wound with a cloth and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause this pain."
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears at the site, or some other kind of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the thighbone or shoulderbone, or other similar ones from large limbs, do not pull it out, for many die from this. Let it be until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Perhaps it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	But if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	"of the bruises that come on the sore"
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often hear questions about the health of fractures, especially when they are near a joint, and it is unpleasant to see the limb misfigured;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore, take heed if the bone is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If the administrator applies medicines that are astringent, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, ache, and similar others, then take some of these things, or all together, and combine them with astringent wine or with abundance of egg yolk or with honey;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	And place them on the bone in bandages, securing it well, and do not remove the bandages for many days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	Then dislocate it again, and begin another one, until the dislocation is removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	Or press on a well-made splint;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	For the property of wood is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	And if the dislocation has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut above it, and remove the excess.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	When you apply it to any razor, until it is removed, and the treatment continues until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	"of the limb which becomes weak after the treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When a bone fracture has been reset, but afterwards the limb remains weak and slender, this happens due to many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bindings, preventing the limb from receiving proper nourishment;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or due to excessive rubbing.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of excessive movement, not done at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because there is little blood in their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment for this is to have the patient eat well and exercise their body until their blood is increased within them;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, giving them joy and ease.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply pitch to the limb so that it attracts great nourishment, and rub it often with cold water until the nourishment reaches the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	"of the limb twisted after the healing"
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone breaks openly, even though it loses its natural shape, its function remains unchanged:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	So do not believe those fools who say that one should break the limb anew, for many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	And such actions are blameworthy, and they cause great harm, and sometimes death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the joints and ligaments are fresh, they should be raised with hot water or mollifying herbs boiled in it, such as fig leaves, roots, and meadowsweet, among others;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a soft plaster using diacathylon or similar, and take the mucilage of figs, mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you can take ripe figs, grind them with fennel seeds and similar medications that soften the joint.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation occurs due to prolonged and continuous rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange for gentle movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the crookedness is hardened and made rigid like stone, it must be cut out with iron; thus one should cut down to the bone gently with a fine incision tool.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put effort and skill into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint is displaced from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the sufferer feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, it must now be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	But if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps it is not reset properly.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	So one should not move it until the swelling has subsided:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times this causes pain and other discomforts;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	Nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient sweat, then let him rest until the inflammation has subsided;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb with warm water and oil, gently reset it, and care for each limb as it comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have arranged chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	Of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It sometimes happens that the lower jaw becomes dislocated inward, and the dislocation of both jaws occurs in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	either they are slightly displaced from their places and softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	If they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the shoulder, and saliva flows from his mouth so that he cannot hold it in or close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it returns by itself with more dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and full, then you must reset it quickly, without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and do it in such a way that the assistants hold the patient's head, and the doctor places one hand behind the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth if the dislocation is on both sides.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	And let his other two hands be free to apply pressure evenly;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften and move his jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the master will put it back in place until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reset is painful, especially if both jaws are dislocated together, then heat them with warm water and oil until they can be reset easily.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not delay in resetting them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then place moistened cloths made of a poultice of rose oil and wax on top, then bind it gently with soft linen.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient lie on their back, with two pillows supporting their head so they do not move to the right or left nor try to chew, but rather consume soft food until the pains are gone and the jaw is healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then they may eat what they wish easily, and need not exert themselves to open their mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is fully healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if both jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fever and chills will ensue, and sometimes diarrhea, and sometimes vomiting of bile alone.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, know that it is useless.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many have died from this in nine days.
de la forcelle	Jaw dislocations are treated using forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The jaw cannot be dislocated on the side towards its continuity with the ear, and sometimes it is dislocated backwards, which can be felt distinctly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the treatment is that the patient lies often on their back with arms extended;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	Then press firmly with your palm to the spot, and it will return
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then place over the emplacement and wrap with bandages, and bind it tight;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	And the head that faces towards the side cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it dislocates even once, then reset it to its place as we have said
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place over the emplacement and wrap with bandages, and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder dislocates in only three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	the first way is when it dislocates towards the part of the hip below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second way is towards the side of the breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes it may dislocate upwards, but this happens rarely
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and the shoulder does not dislocate backwards nor does it dislocate inwards for the nerves
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And often dislocated downwards towards the buttock, especially for those who have flesh on their bones, as it happens suddenly.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those with sufficient flesh, it scarcely happens and scarcely goes back in place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes in certain men there is injury or fracture, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with heat and swelling, and they believe that it has been dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You must therefore examine it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocations are when they are downwards towards the buttock, and there is a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, which you will find clearly different;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And at the head of the shoulder you will find a hollow, and below the buttock upon touching the head of the shoulder it will feel like an egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And the patient cannot bring their hand close to their neck nor move it in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	Also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden because you will find it clearly upon touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation cannot be reduced, especially when it is recent or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his fingers under the shoulder blade, and lifts the joint with force upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister lifts up the hand and extends it outwards, then places it underneath.
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within several days afterwards, then the patient must be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister should apply gently softening and soothing ointments, such as a decoction of ale and fennel and melilot in water, and it should be applied;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on their back, and under the shoulder blade a pillow of even linen, not too soft nor too hard, then the master places his heel on the pillow, lifts up the head of the shoulder gently, and draws out the patient's hand;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister holds the patient's head so that it does not move downwards.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	This shoulder has returned entirely dislocated, and if you see it, reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and make sure that a man who is taller than the patient is present;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and let him stand straight beside the cost side, and place his shoulder beneath the patient's hip, lifting the hip upwards so that the patient hangs by the armpit;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And another servant pulls the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang something heavy on him, and the dislocation will return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also reset in this other manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that one places a long stake in the ground, such that the head of the shoulder is as high as the fist, and not too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then one places it beneath the patient, but let there be soft cloths underneath, and the patient stands along the length of the stake
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then stretch his hand down on the other side properly, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not want to return because of all these things that we have said, do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a splint of 2 cubits long and 4 fingers wide, which has a round head so that it can enter deeply under the armpit, as follows:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then wrap the splinted wood around the shoulder below so that it does not burn or harm the patient. Then place it under the armpit of the patient.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	Stretch out the arm on the wooden support and tie the shoulder to it. Then put the arm on a sling made from a cloth of suitable width. Let the hand hang downwards and let the body hang freely on the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint is now in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever way this may be, then you must put under the armpit a wad of wool equal in size; then place on the shoulder the emplastrum prepared with powder from the millstone, with incense and albumen of egg all around; then draw it under the armpit gradually, and turn the bandage over the emplastrum, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let it remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And he should eat little until the limb is comfortable again for it will heal more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	Then eat more after five or seven days and move the arm.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	If it is firm and softened again, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is removed from its place due to moisture that has come there or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries with three holes, as it is shown before in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this and after seven days the dislocation still occurs, and he cannot lift his arm up again, know that the nerves of the shoulder head are either cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And know that the joint will never again be set right.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that occurs toward the arm and breasts or behind is caused by forceful impact and extension of limbs, whereupon one applies another restraint.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat it until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the member and slowness in movement, then the sick person should take many baths until that pain is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated easily and easily returns to its position.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And if it has been dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, the dislocation will not remain unseen or unnoticed.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Dislocated according to each position.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder completely.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it before an abscess forms there, for if an abscess were to form, it would be difficult to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	Indeed, it may not always be possible to fully reset it, especially when it is dislocated behind the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	So this dislocation is worse than others and causes more pain, and sometimes death occurs.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And its restoration is such that, if it can be reset, you stretch out his hand with both of your hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arms should be spread out, and the hands of the surgeon placed along the elbow on top and bottom, and push the joint into his fingers together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forwards, then it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and pushes the neck that is dislocated from the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	And two ministers should extend the arm, and two ministers should hold it so that it does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then twist the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth doubly around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the surgeon has joined the joint with his hand, then he should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, and then forcefully push the joint until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, then put on a dry compress with egg yolk, and bind it tightly, and hang the arm around the neck of the patient, leaving it for some days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie it and leave it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint is not properly aligned, then recommence the emplacement and untie it, leaving it thus for a few days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	Then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if there is great pain after the resetting of the joint and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it and press until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you put on the joint a poultice of fat mutton, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter into a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when it sweats, if you gently rub the joint, then put back on the poultice and then enter the bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus twice or thrice until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	And if you see that, then put on fine wet hay heated with butter and bind it.
si revenra a sa disposition.	If it returns to its position
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocated shoulder joint, and its return is easy, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it must be reset promptly to its place, in the very opening where it was dislocated, before the area becomes inflamed or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is thus: place the affected hand on a table, extend the minister's hand, and the physician places theirs evenly, so that their palm presses against the front of the joint, pushing until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Still, you must ensure it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the physician places his hand on the surface of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply cold compresses to soothe any heat and swelling, and allow it to rest without beginning again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if the patient cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back into place after several days, then the joint remains dislocated;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	And let not even fire harm the patient unless his hand is weakened, and he cannot grasp anything entirely.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then know that the nerves are cut or the artery.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other means of heat than to burn with fire nearby the case, and sometimes nothing else may help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then remove it and leave it so."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply warm water poultice, and rub it until it becomes flexible."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	"On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes both hands are dislocated at each end, sometimes at the back of the palm or the front.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then stretch out your hands, and push the dislocation back into its socket until it returns, then hold the head of the hand, and bend it towards the side where it was dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	And leave it for two days, and on the third day make it even.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And withhold the food as we have said, both during the day of the dislocation and the following days, but do not move it and tie it up.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And likewise when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	"On the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back"
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	"If the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocations, then there is no remedy, for death quickly ensues."
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the sign of this is that the evacuations come forth involuntarily and cannot be retained, and often some limbs become softened, especially the two thighs or the two arms.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And oftentimes the backbone moves in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves at the rear is called 'gilbositez':
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is: if the gilbositez has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	There is no remedy nor healing for it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or blow or similar things, the old authors spoke of various treatments with grand words, but they have little benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have summarized it according to my intention and have formed instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that there is no remedy nor healing for the gilbositez that comes at the breast before;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also that which comes straight into both sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes properly at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	It is necessary for the patient to lie upon their back on a flat surface, with something underneath them so that they do not bruise themselves.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then firmly plant one poker at the head and another at the feet on the ground, bind a rope tightly around the patient's thighs, then at the hips, knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two assistants hold the ropes, one at the head and another at the feet, between the two pokers
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be securely closed with the poker as we have described, then the physician places their palms firmly on the spine until it yields.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if the spine does not yield with this treatment, then take a board three spans long and place it under the patient's back while they are on their side, and put one end of the board under the spine, then place the middle of the board on the spine
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and the physician places their feet on the other end of the board and presses firmly until the spine yields to its proper place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see one, do it on the shoulder that rotates towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is necessary that you insert two stakes at the head of the sick person's arm, and towards the feet two others; and there should be between each stake, above and below, a palm's length of space.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and let there be one hole in each stake where the shoulder rotates, and let the stakes be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each of the two stakes let there be one turning stake, over which the sling rotates, and let there be in both turnings two small stakes a palm's length long, for turning the shoulder.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the sling that is among the stakes to the shoulder stake towards the head, and the other sling towards the feet at the other stake; and each of the assistants should turn their stake for all the sling, and the master shall place the sling evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then place a drying plaster with plenty of egg on it, and then the compresses, and then the pestle of a tablet three fingers long, which should press upon the location of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a linen bandage, as we have said, and let the patient use gentle nourishment until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if something comes to prevent recovery at the end of healing, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines with the pestle that we mentioned earlier.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes one administers a piece of flax, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and it is thought that this may be dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone which opens, therefore one must not presume there.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	"Dislocations of the hip"
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that in the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder, there come forth only dislocations, not like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the articulation of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	Inside and outside, front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	And more so inside than others, especially the dislocation before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee opens more than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in front of the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the place that is near is swollen with hot abscess because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one whom it happens outside is that this accident is opposite to those in front
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the sign of one who has it in front is that their leg is well stretched according to its completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot move forward, and he retains his urine, and the angle swells, and when he walks, he drags his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one whom it happens behind is that he cannot straighten or bend his knee, and this leg is twisted compared to the other; the ankle is softened, and the bone of the thigh is located below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The reduction of this kind of dislocation is that you wait if the dislocation is ancient, and it remains according to its position, so there is no treatment;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And there must be no presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four kinds of dislocation, you should quickly reposition the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	Perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and stretch the leg strongly with both hands, or tie it to something above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another assistant extends his hand in such a way that he places his hands under the buttocks, then tightly binds it with a soft rope above the hip.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another holds the end of the rope.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	Then everyone pulls up and down at once so that the patient is lifted off the ground all at once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching applies to four types of dislocation. If the dislocation has returned [to its normal position], as we have said, that is good
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then treat it according to its similarity.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is at the hip joint, you should lay the patient on their healthy side, then place the rope at the root of the hip and under the angle, then pull the rope up towards the angle and towards the thigh.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another helper's arms, and embrace the hip bone of the sick person tightly, and stretch it towards the front strongly:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	And now it will return to its place:
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	This manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have described, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a soft rope at both heels and knees, and let the sick leg extend two fingers more than the other:
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then hang it over the top of a stick, and raise it two arm-lengths above the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command one helper to embrace the top of the hip bone, and have another helper hang with the patient, embracing the hip bone strongly, for the joint will now quickly return.
